* nelisp-emacs pure standalone reader resume
:PROPERTIES:
:DATE: 2026-06-02
:PROJECT: /home/madblack-21/Cowork/Notes/dev/nelisp-emacs
:STATUS: resumed
:END:

Development resumed from the 2026-05-27 checkpoint after NeLisp moved
to the zero-Rust pure-Elisp standalone reader.

** Context

The old checkpoint blocker was `make doctor' failing at the legacy
`target/release/nelisp eval (identity 42)' path.  The sibling NeLisp
checkout now provides `target/nelisp-standalone-reader', whose command
surface is different: it loads an `.el' file and reports the low byte of
the last integer value as the process exit code.

** Implemented

- `Makefile' now resolves `NELISP_BIN' to
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader' first, with
  `target/release/nelisp' retained as a compatibility fallback.
- `bin/nemacs' now resolves NeLisp with the same preference order.
- `bin/nemacs --doctor' recognizes the standalone-reader driver and
  verifies literal/list eval through its exit-code contract:
  - `42' -> exit 42
  - `(+ 40 2)' -> exit 42
- Legacy CLI doctor behavior remains in place for older checkouts.
- `make test-nelisp' now distinguishes the standalone reader from the
  legacy command CLI.  For `nelisp-standalone-reader' it runs a
  file-based `(+ 40 2)' smoke and expects exit 42, then runs
  `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp --batch' through the same reader; for the
  legacy CLI it keeps the existing `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp --eval'
  smoke.
- Runtime-image make targets now use `NELISP_LEGACY_CLI' explicitly and
  fail early with a clear message because `nelisp-standalone-reader'
  does not provide `dump-runtime-image', `extend-runtime-image', or
  `eval FORM' command surfaces yet.
- `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp' now captures the standalone-reader exit
  status without letting `set -e' skip cleanup, so temporary boot
  scripts are removed even when the reader exits nonzero.
- `bin/build-nelisp' now builds the zero-Rust
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader' via NeLisp's `make
  standalone-reader' path by default.  The old Cargo-built CLI is an
  explicit `NELISP_BUILD_LEGACY_CLI=1' compatibility option.
- Added `verify-nelisp-standalone' as the current pure reader gate:
  `doctor', `test-nelisp', and `verify-vendor-class-a'.
- README guidance now describes standalone-reader first and the old CLI
  as a compatibility fallback.
- README command examples and `make help' initially labelled
  `profile-nelisp-bootstrap' and `diagnose-vendor-form-walk' as
  legacy-CLI diagnostics rather than standalone-reader lanes; the later
  continuation below supersedes that for current checkouts.
- Added shell-wrapper coverage for the standalone-reader doctor path,
  file-based `--batch -l/--eval' boot script generation, runtime-image
  rejection, and nonzero cleanup.

** Verification

#+begin_example
bash -n bin/nemacs
bash -n bin/build-nelisp
NELISP_VENDOR_DIR=../nelisp bin/build-nelisp --no-pull
git diff --check

emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L demo --eval '(setq load-prefer-newer t native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-main-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "shell-wrapper")'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq load-prefer-newer t native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-vendor-core")'
make test EMACS="emacs --batch --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)'"
#+end_example

  `STANDALONE-READER=ok exit=42' and
  `NEMACS-STANDALONE-BOOT=ok exit=0'.
- `make verify-vendor-class-a' and `make verify-nelisp-standalone'
  passed on the standalone reader path.
- Targeted shell-wrapper and Makefile runtime-image ERTs passed.
- Host ERT passed:
  - 1541 tests
  - 1532 expected results
  - 0 unexpected
  - 9 intentional skips

Note: plain targeted ERT without disabling native-comp subr trampolines
failed before the test selector ran, while loading `emacs-stub.el', with
the host Emacs native-comp error `Type number missing from typeof-types!'.
The same tests pass when `native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines' is nil.

three-step gate.

** Continuation: standalone diagnostics migration

`profile-nelisp-bootstrap' and `diagnose-vendor-form-walk' no longer
require the legacy command CLI when `target/nelisp-standalone-reader' is
available.

Implemented:

- Added `scripts/standalone-bootstrap-profile.el'.  Host Emacs splits
  the generated `build/nemacs-bootstrap.el' bundle by its source section
  markers, writes cumulative standalone-reader probe files, appends a
  success sentinel, and reports host-measured elapsed time per section.
  This avoids depending on standalone-reader stdout.
- Added `scripts/vendor-form-standalone-walk.el'.  Host Emacs parses a
  vendor file into top-level forms, writes cumulative standalone-reader
  probe files with the bootstrap bundle and a success sentinel, and
  reports the first form whose run does not reach that sentinel.
- `Makefile' now routes `profile-nelisp-bootstrap' and
  `diagnose-vendor-form-walk' through the standalone-reader helpers when
  `NELISP_BIN' resolves to `nelisp-standalone-reader'.  The legacy CLI
  paths remain compatibility fallbacks for older checkouts.
- README guidance now describes profile/form-walk as standalone-reader
  diagnostics and leaves runtime-image commands as the remaining legacy
  CLI lane.
- Added host ERT coverage for the new diagnostic helpers and for the
  Makefile standalone diagnostic routing.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make profile-nelisp-bootstrap NELISP_BOOT_PROFILE_LIMIT=2
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile")'
#+end_example

Results:

- `make profile-nelisp-bootstrap NELISP_BOOT_PROFILE_LIMIT=2' passed on
  the standalone-reader path and reported section timings for
  `src/emacs-fns.el' and `src/emacs-eval.el'.
- `make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1' now runs on
  the standalone-reader path and reports the current blocker:
  `vendor/emacs-lisp/simple.el' form 1, head `eval-when-compile',

- `standalone-diagnostics-test.el' passed: 4 tests, 4 expected,

** Continuation: bootstrap segfaults cleared through simple.el form 428

The previous `simple.el' form-1 blocker was a bootstrap-load false
positive: `build/nemacs-bootstrap.el' itself still crashed once the full
bundle was loaded before the vendor form.

Implemented:

- `emacs-stub-bulk.el' now marks generated no-op function and macro
  stubs with the `emacs-stub-bulk' symbol property when it installs
  them.  Later real shims can detect bulk placeholders without calling
  them.
- `emacs-stub.el' and `emacs-time.el' now replace a marked bulk
  `truncate' without executing the old stub.  Their standalone
  bootstrap body also avoids float literals and `while' in the early
  `truncate' definition, because standalone-reader can segfault while
  installing that shape.
- `emacs-numeric.el' keeps host `atan' / `exp' untouched, but replaces
  marked bulk stubs with constant standalone bootstrap fallbacks.  This
  avoids the float-literal comparison body that crashed while installing
  the old interpreted approximation.
- Added host ERT coverage for marked-bulk replacement of `truncate',
  `atan', and `exp'.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/emacs-time-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/emacs-numeric-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'

** Continuation: normalized vendor form diagnostic

The raw standalone vendor form walker intentionally still reports the
real blocker at `vendor/emacs-lisp/simple.el' form 429.  To keep
exploring later vendor forms without hiding that raw failure, the
standalone diagnostic now has an explicit normalization mode.

Implemented:

- Added `VENDOR_FORM_WALK_NORMALIZE_FLOATS=t' for
  `diagnose-vendor-form-walk' on the standalone-reader path.
- Added `vendor-form-standalone-normalize-floats'.  When non-nil, the
  host-side probe rewrites float literals in each top-level vendor form
  to truncated integers before writing the temporary standalone-reader
  program.
- The default remains raw vendor source (`nil'), so the diagnostic still
  identifies the exact unmodified vendor form that crashes.
- Added ERT coverage that float normalization is opt-in.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_NORMALIZE_FLOATS=t
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=180 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=45 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_NORMALIZE_FLOATS=t
make verify-nelisp-standalone
make test EMACS="emacs --batch --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)'"
git diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- `standalone-diagnostics-test.el' passed: 5 tests, 5 expected,

- Raw `diagnose-vendor-form-walk' still fails at `simple.el' form 429,
  `line-move-partial', with `"Segmentation fault"', preserving the exact
  standalone-reader blocker.
- With `VENDOR_FORM_WALK_NORMALIZE_FLOATS=t', form 429 reaches the
  sentinel.
- With normalization enabled, forms 429-608 reach the sentinel; combined
  with the previous raw 1-428 walk, all `simple.el' top-level forms are
  explorable under the diagnostic.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed.
- Full host ERT passed: 1549 tests, 1540 expected results,
  0 unexpected, 9 intentional skips.

   comparison/install crash surfaced by `simple.el' form 429,
   `line-move-partial'.  The normalized diagnostic is only a follow-on
   exploration tool, not a replacement for fixing the raw reader crash.

** Continuation: raw reader float materialization fixed

The raw `simple.el' form-429 blocker was not specific to
`line-move-partial'.  A file containing only `1.0' also segfaulted under
`target/nelisp-standalone-reader', which narrowed the failure to the
reader float token path rather than to bootstrap or vendor form shape.

Root cause in the sibling `nelisp' checkout:

- The reader build linked `nl_sexp_write_float' as a never-run stub.
- That stub wrote Sexp tag `9', which is the boxed CharTable tag, not
  tag `3' for inline Float.
- When `nl_eval_inner' self-evaluated the result, `nl_sexp_clone_into'
  treated the value as a boxed CharTable and read the f64 payload bits as
  a pointer, causing the standalone segfault.

Implemented in sibling `../nelisp':

- Replaced the Phase47 stub in `scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el' with
  a tiny raw link unit exporting `nl_sexp_write_float'.
- The raw unit writes tag `3', copies the f64 payload from `xmm0' into
  slot offset 8, clears offsets 16 and 24, and returns the slot pointer.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader
target/nelisp-standalone-reader /tmp/one-float.el
make standalone-reader-test
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=180 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=45
make verify-nelisp-standalone
#+end_example

Results:

- A raw file containing only `1.0' no longer segfaults.
- `(if (floatp 1.0) 42 13)' and `(if (numberp 1.0) 42 13)'
  both exit 42 under the standalone reader.
- Raw `simple.el' form 429 now reaches the sentinel.
- Raw `simple.el' forms 429-608 now reach the sentinel; combined with
  the previous raw 1-428 pass, all top-level forms in `simple.el' have
  now been walked without float normalization.
- `make standalone-reader-test' passed after rerunning without a
  concurrent binary execution.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed, including
  `VENDOR_CORE_LIMIT=0' via the standalone reader.

Known residual:

- Mixed integer/float numeric comparison is still incomplete:
  `(if (>= 2 1.0) 42 13)' currently exits 13.  That is now a numeric
  semantics gap, not the raw reader crash.

*** Next resume point

1. Runtime-image bake/replay targets still require the legacy CLI because
   standalone-reader has no working file-write/image command surface yet.
2. The previous raw `simple.el' form 429 crash is fixed.  Next standalone
   vendor work should move from crash bypassing to either mixed numeric
   semantics or the next full-vendor/load barrier beyond the daily-driver
   vendor-core gate.

** Continuation: mixed int/float comparison fixed

The raw float materialization fix exposed the next numeric semantics gap:
the standalone reader could now read and self-evaluate floats, but the
pure-Elisp builtin dispatcher still compared numeric payload words as
integers.  For Float values, that word is the IEEE754 bit pattern, so
mixed predicates such as `(>= 2 1.0)' returned nil.

Implemented in sibling `../nelisp':

- Updated `scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el' applyfn comparison arms
  for `=', `<', `>', `<=', and `>=' to dispatch through tag-aware
  numeric helpers.
- The helpers keep the existing integer fast path when both operands are
  Ints.
- If either operand is Float, Int operands are converted with
  `i64-to-f64' and Float operands are unwrapped with
  `sexp-float-unwrap' + `bits-to-f64', then compared with the existing
  Phase47 `f64-lt' / `f64-gt' / `f64-le' / `f64-ge' emitters.
- `=' is implemented as numeric `<= && >=' so `1' and `1.0' compare
  equal without using the epsilon-only helper.
- `eq' now checks both tag and payload word so type-mismatched immediate
  values such as `0' and `0.0' are no longer accidentally true.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader
target/nelisp-standalone-reader /tmp/mixed-numeric-probe.el
make standalone-reader-test
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=429 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=180 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=60
make verify-nelisp-standalone
#+end_example

Direct probe results:

- `(if (>= 2 1.0) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (>= 0 1.0) 42 13)' exits 13.
- `(if (< 1 2.0) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (> 1.5 1) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (<= 1 1.0) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (= 1 1.0) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (= 1 2.0) 42 13)' exits 13.
- `(if (eq 0 0.0) 42 13)' exits 13.
- `(if (eq 7 7) 42 13)' exits 42.

Gate results:

- `make standalone-reader-test' passed.
- Raw `simple.el' forms 429-608 still reach the sentinel.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed, including the full
  `VENDOR_CORE_LIMIT=0' standalone vendor-core lane.

*** Next resume point

1. Runtime-image bake/replay targets still require the legacy CLI because
   standalone-reader has no working file-write/image command surface yet.
2. The float reader crash and mixed int/float comparison gap are fixed.
   Next standalone vendor work should move to the next full-vendor/load
   barrier beyond the daily-driver vendor-core gate, or to widening the
   runtime-image command surface in the standalone reader.

** Continuation: UTF-8 char literals unblocked lisp-mode form-walk

Raw standalone vendor form-walk was extended beyond the daily-driver
vendor-core gate.  `simple.el', `files.el', `dired.el', `help-mode.el',
`help-fns.el', `subr-x.el', `seq.el', `map.el', `lisp.el', and `ielm.el'
had already reached their sentinels.  The next barrier was:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/lisp-mode.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=24 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
#+end_example

It failed at top-level form 24:

#+begin_example
(defconst lisp-prettify-symbols-alist '(("lambda" . ?λ))
  "Alist of symbol/\"pretty\" characters to be displayed.")
#+end_example

Root cause in sibling `../nelisp':

- `lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-lexer.el' treated plain `?X' character
  literals as exactly one source byte.
- `?λ' is a two-byte UTF-8 sequence, so the lexer emitted only the
  first byte as the char payload and left the second byte to be parsed
  as the next token.
- `lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-parser.el' also decoded plain char payloads by
  returning byte 0 directly, so non-ASCII codepoints could not be
  materialized on the pure AOT reader path.

Implemented in sibling `../nelisp':

- Added UTF-8 leading-byte width detection to the reader lexer for
  plain non-escaped `?X' char literals.
- The lexer now pushes the full 1/2/3/4-byte UTF-8 codepoint payload.
- Added parser-side UTF-8 codepoint decoding for 1/2/3/4-byte payloads.
- Added `?λ' to `nelisp-standalone--prelude-breadth-test-src' so the
  standalone reader prelude breadth gate covers this path.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader
target/nelisp-standalone-reader /tmp/nelisp-char-probe.el
make standalone-reader-test
make standalone-reader-prelude-test
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/lisp-mode.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=24 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/lisp-mode.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=25
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/isearch.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=100
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/minibuffer.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=100
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/progmodes/project.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=75
make verify-nelisp-standalone
#+end_example

Results:

- `(if (= ?a 97) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(if (= ?λ 955) 42 13)' exits 42.
- `(quote (("lambda" . ?λ)))' followed by sentinel `42' exits 42.
- `make standalone-reader-test' passed.
- `make standalone-reader-prelude-test' passed, including the new `?λ'
  breadth check.
- Raw `lisp-mode.el' form 24 now reaches the sentinel.
- Raw `lisp-mode.el' all 99 forms reach the sentinel.
- Raw `isearch.el' all 344 forms reach the sentinel.
- Raw `minibuffer.el' all 275 forms reach the sentinel.
- Raw `project.el' all 146 forms reach the sentinel.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed, including the full
  `VENDOR_CORE_LIMIT=0' standalone vendor-core lane.

*** Next resume point

1. Runtime-image bake/replay targets still require the legacy CLI because
   standalone-reader has no working file-write/image command surface yet.
2. The current raw cumulative form-walk now covers the daily-driver
   vendor-core target set plus `lisp-mode.el', `isearch.el',
   `minibuffer.el', and `project.el'.  Next standalone vendor work should
   either try true file-load replay for these modules, widen the runtime
   image command surface, or continue raw form-walk toward larger
   remaining vendor modules.

** Continuation: standalone vendor load replay diagnostic

The raw cumulative form-walk confirmed that several larger vendor files
can be evaluated when their top-level forms are embedded directly after
`build/nemacs-bootstrap.el'.  The next question was whether the same
surface works through true file loading on the standalone-reader path.

Manual probes showed an important shape constraint:

- `(progn (load ".../build/nemacs-bootstrap.el" nil 'no-message t t) 42)'
  exits 0 under the standalone reader.
- The same load as a top-level form followed by a separate top-level
  `42' exits 42.

So the replay diagnostic intentionally writes top-level `load' forms,
not one large `progn'.  This matches the standalone reader's multi-form
driver and avoids hiding success behind a large nested form.

Implemented:

- Added `scripts/vendor-load-standalone-replay.el'.
- Added `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay'.
- The target builds/uses `build/nemacs-bootstrap.el', then generates a
  temporary standalone-reader script that sets `nelisp-emacs-vendor-root',
  sets `load-path', top-level-loads the bootstrap bundle, top-level-loads
  every file in `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES', and finally evaluates sentinel `42'.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' covers the current larger follow-up set:
  `lisp-mode.el', `isearch.el', `minibuffer.el', and `project.el'.
- Added ERT coverage in `test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el' for file
  list parsing and the top-level-load program shape.
- Extended the Makefile diagnostics ERT so the new target stays on the
  standalone-reader helper path.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
#+end_example

Results:

- `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' passed with exit 42 after true
  top-level `load' replay of `lisp-mode.el', `isearch.el',
  `minibuffer.el', and `project.el'.
- `standalone-diagnostics-test.el' passed: 7/7 tests.
- `nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test/makefile-diagnostics-prefer-standalone-reader'
  passed.

*** Next resume point

1. Runtime-image bake/replay targets still require the legacy CLI because
   standalone-reader has no `dump-runtime-image' / `extend-runtime-image'
   command surface.
2. The standalone-reader path now has three useful vendor diagnostics:
   bootstrap prefix profiling, raw cumulative form-walk, and true
   top-level vendor load replay.  Next work should either:
   - add `diagnose-vendor-load-replay' to a broader verification lane once
     its cost/noise is acceptable,
   - continue true load replay toward more vendor files, or
   - start widening standalone-reader commands for runtime-image output.

** Correction: load replay proof and vendor-core gate honesty

The first `diagnose-vendor-load-replay' implementation only checked that
the final sentinel was reached.  A stronger probe showed that this was
insufficient:

#+begin_example
(load ".../build/nemacs-bootstrap.el" nil 'no-message t t)
(if (fboundp 'emacs-keymap-define-key-after) 42 13)
#+end_example

This exits 13 under the current standalone reader, and loading a missing
file followed by `42' also exits 42.  In other words, the standalone
multi-form driver can continue after a failed/unimplemented `load', so a
bare trailing sentinel is a false positive for true file-load replay.

Implemented:

- `scripts/vendor-load-standalone-replay.el' now writes a final
  `(if VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM 42 13)' instead of a bare `42'.
- `Makefile' now exposes `VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM', defaulting to
  `(fboundp (quote emacs-keymap-define-key-after))' to prove that the
  bootstrap bundle was actually evaluated.
- The standalone `verify-vendor-core' branch no longer depends on
  `(load scripts/vendor-core-standalone-gate.el ...)'.  It now embeds
  `build/nemacs-bootstrap.el' and `scripts/vendor-core-smoke.el' into
  the temporary standalone-reader script and expects exit 42.  This keeps
  the gate honest while `load' is not a working command surface.
- Updated ERT coverage for the proof form and the embedded vendor-core
  smoke Makefile shape.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make verify-vendor-core
make verify-nelisp-standalone
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay   # expected current failure: exit 13
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-standalone")'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
#+end_example

Results:

- `make verify-vendor-core' passed with `VENDOR-CORE-STANDALONE=ok
  exit=42' using the embedded smoke script.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed with the corrected
  `verify-vendor-core' branch.
- `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' now fails as expected with exit 13,
  proving the current true `load' command surface is still missing.
- `standalone-diagnostics-test.el' passed: 7/7 tests.
- The targeted Makefile ERTs passed for both `makefile-standalone' and
  `makefile-diagnostics'.

*** Next resume point

1. Runtime-image bake/replay still require the legacy CLI because
   standalone-reader has no `dump-runtime-image' / `extend-runtime-image'
   command surface.
2. The standalone-reader vendor-core gate is now an honest embedded
   smoke rather than a `load' false positive.
3. The next real command-surface task is implementing or wiring `load'
   for standalone-reader so `diagnose-vendor-load-replay' can pass its
   proof form, then extending that toward runtime-image commands.

** True standalone `load' replay now reaches the default vendor set

Implemented in sibling `nelisp':

- Added standalone-reader `load' to the builtin install list and
  dispatch table.
- `bf_load' now reads the target file, parses each top-level form with
  the pure reader, and evaluates it in the caller's environment.
- Added `set', `featurep', `provide', and `require' builtins needed by
  the standalone prelude/bootstrap load path.
- `bf_load' disables arena free-list reuse before file loads.  Bootstrap
  leaves enough dead/reusable blocks that a later large vector allocation
  could otherwise reuse unsafe storage and segfault; disabling reuse keeps
  this command surface correctness-first.

Implemented in `nelisp-emacs':

- `diagnose-vendor-load-replay' now loads
  `VENDOR_LOAD_PRELUDE' before `build/nemacs-bootstrap.el'.
- `help-mode--standalone-p' now uses the explicit
  `nelisp-emacs-vendor-root' marker, because both `emacs-version' and
  `file-truename' can be defined by the bootstrap before `help-mode.el'.
- Added standalone load-time stubs for `define-abbrev-table',
  `make-syntax-table', `modify-syntax-entry', `let-when-compile', and
  `defvar-keymap'.
- `defface' keeps the full host/regular bridge, but under standalone
  vendor replay registers only the face symbol to avoid expanding large
  face specs during load diagnostics.
- `bin/nemacs' now disables native-comp subr trampolines for its
  host-batch doctor probe and bootstrap form.  This keeps the clean host
  Emacs path from failing in `button.el' before the standalone checks run.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make verify-nelisp-standalone
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay

make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=.../isearch.el
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=.../minibuffer.el
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=.../progmodes/project.el
make standalone-reader-test
make standalone-reader-prelude-test
make verify-vendor-core
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-standalone")'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
git diff --check   # both nelisp-emacs and sibling nelisp
#+end_example

Results:

- Default `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' passed: the standalone
  reader loaded the prelude, bootstrap bundle, `lisp-mode.el',
  `isearch.el', `minibuffer.el', and `project.el', then exited 42 via the
  proof form.
- Each default vendor file also passed as a single-file replay.
- Sibling `make standalone-reader-test' and
  `make standalone-reader-prelude-test' passed after cleaning the
  generated standalone unit cache.  The first parallel attempt produced a
  batch lock conflict and a corrupt unit-cache read; the sequential rerun
  after `make standalone-eval-clean' passed.
- `make verify-vendor-core' passed with `VENDOR-CORE-STANDALONE=ok
  exit=42'.
- The standalone diagnostics ERT passed 7/7; the targeted Makefile ERTs
  passed for `makefile-standalone' and `makefile-diagnostics'.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed.  The gate now proves `doctor',
  `test-nelisp', `verify-vendor-class-a', and `verify-vendor-core' with
  the standalone-reader driver.
- `./bin/nemacs --doctor' also passed directly with the standalone-reader
  driver after the host-batch native-comp trampoline setting was applied.

** Standalone runtime-image bake/replay lane is on the source-v1 path

Implemented in sibling `nelisp':

- Added standalone-reader runtime-image command detection for
  `dump-runtime-image', `extend-runtime-image', `eval-runtime-image', and
  `exec-runtime-image' by comparing argv C strings before the normal file
  source selection.
- Embedded the standalone prelude plus `lisp/nelisp-runtime-image.el' as
  the runtime-image command source and exposed `nelisp-standalone-argv' to
  that command source.
- Added the file/output builtins needed by the runtime-image helper:
  `nl-write-file', `nelisp--write-stdout-bytes',
  `nelisp--write-stderr-line', and `nelisp--eval-source-string'.
- `nelisp-runtime-image.el' now uses the standalone eval-source helper
  when available, uses `rdf' for standalone file reads, and avoids the
  post-dump validation eval on the standalone dump path.  The validation
  command frame is still unstable, while the written source-v1 image is
  replayable through the normal file-eval path.

Implemented in `nelisp-emacs':

- Runtime-image Makefile lanes now use `NELISP_BIN' instead of forcing
  `NELISP_LEGACY_CLI'.  The old guard saying standalone-reader had no
  `dump-runtime-image' / `extend-runtime-image' command surface was
  removed.
- `bin/nemacs' now handles standalone-reader `--runtime-image' by
  prepending the `.nlri' source to the temporary boot script, appending
  the normal boot form, and adding a final `0' sentinel.  This keeps
  runtime replay on the stable source-file path instead of relying on
  direct standalone `exec-runtime-image'.
- Shell-wrapper ERT now proves that a standalone runtime image file is
  prepended to the captured boot script.
- README now documents that source-v1 runtime images are replay bundles,
  not startup accelerators, and that direct standalone
  `exec-runtime-image' remains diagnostic-only.

Verification:

emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile")'
#+end_example

** Interactive and vendor-core runtime-image lanes pass on standalone replay

Follow-up from the previous section:

- `make test-nelisp-interactive-runtime-image' passed with
  `NEMACS_INTERACTIVE_RUNTIME_IMAGE=build/nemacs-interactive-runtime-standalone-smoke.nlri'.

  replay path.

  `extend-runtime-image' when extending the full nemacs batch base image.
  The same base image plus `(nemacs-runtime-image-preload-vendor-core-extension)'

  isolated to nested command-frame validation, not to the source-v1 image
  payload.
- Sibling `nelisp' was updated so standalone `extend-runtime-image'
  mirrors the standalone `dump-runtime-image' policy: write the source-v1

  frame.  Legacy CLI/non-standalone still validates before writing.

  small source-v1 images exit 0, but full nemacs images that contain
  `load' still exit 1 in the direct command frame.  The supported
  full-image path remains `bin/nemacs --runtime-image', which prepends the
  image to a temporary source file and evaluates it through the stable
  file-mode reader path.

variable into earlier non-image smoke steps, so `test-nelisp' tried to

commands now pass `NEMACS_RUNTIME_IMAGE=' explicitly, keeping the command
line variable scoped to the runtime-image target.

** Direct standalone `exec-runtime-image' uses file-mode source replay

The remaining direct-command gap was closed in sibling `nelisp':

- `scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el' now intercepts
  `exec-runtime-image' and `eval-runtime-image' during driver source
  selection.
- Instead of evaluating the image through the embedded runtime-image
  command source, the driver reads argv[2] as the image file, appends
  argv[3] as the requested form, appends a final `0' success sentinel,
  and hands the combined string to the normal multi-form reader loop.
- `dump-runtime-image' and `extend-runtime-image' continue to use the
  embedded runtime-image command source because they need file output.
- `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp --runtime-image FILE' now uses direct
  standalone `exec-runtime-image' again instead of constructing a
  temporary replay file itself.
- Shell-wrapper ERT was updated to assert the direct
  `exec-runtime-image IMAGE BOOT_FORM' invocation.

  silently succeeding.

  probe still passed.

  `exec-runtime-image IMAGE BOOT_FORM' launcher shape.

  `make standalone-reader-prelude-test' passed.

** Direct `eval-runtime-image' prints and accepts `FORM...'

Completion follow-up from the previous section:

- Sibling `nelisp' now keeps direct `exec-runtime-image' and
  `eval-runtime-image' on the normal multi-form source replay route while
  preserving the CLI distinction:
  - `exec-runtime-image IMAGE FORM...' appends every supplied form and a
    final zero sentinel.
  - `eval-runtime-image IMAGE FORM...' evaluates the supplied forms as a
    `progn', prints the final value with `%S' formatting plus newline,
    and then appends a zero sentinel.
- `make standalone-reader-test' in sibling `nelisp' now includes a small
  runtime-image smoke covering `dump-runtime-image',
  multi-form `eval-runtime-image' stdout, multi-form `exec-runtime-image'
  exit behavior, and missing-form `exec-runtime-image' failure.
- `README.org' was updated so the direct eval/exec semantics are no
  longer documented only as exit-code replay.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader-test
../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader eval-runtime-image build/nemacs-runtime-direct-gate4.nlri '42'
../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader eval-runtime-image build/nemacs-runtime-direct-gate4.nlri '(setq x 40)' '(+ x 2)'
../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader exec-runtime-image build/nemacs-runtime-direct-gate4.nlri '(setq x 40)' '(+ x 2)'
#+end_example

Results:

- Sibling `make standalone-reader-test' passed, including the new
  runtime-image smoke.
- Direct full-image `eval-runtime-image' printed `42' and exited 0.
- Direct full-image multi-form `eval-runtime-image' printed `42' and
  exited 0.
- Direct full-image multi-form `exec-runtime-image' exited 0 without
  printing.

** Continuation: NeLisp development REPL prerequisite

For `nelisp-emacs' development, the missing prerequisite was not another
in-process `ielm' clone inside the editor layer.  `src/emacs-ielm.el' and
`src/emacs-elisp-eval.el' already cover the editor UI side.  The useful
missing piece was a persistent NeLisp evaluator process whose environment
survives across entries, so `defun' / `fset' / `setq' changes take effect
immediately while the process keeps running.

Implemented in the sibling `../nelisp' checkout:

- Added `repl [--no-prompt]' to the zero-Rust
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader' driver.  The implementation lives in
  the pure-Elisp Phase47 driver source: it reads stdin via raw
  `syscall-direct' calls, loads the stdlib prelude once at startup, then
  evaluates each line through the same reader/eval loop and the same live
  `ctx'.
- Added `nelisp-standalone--reader-repl-smoke' so
  `make standalone-reader-test' now covers the persistent REPL path,
  `repl --bad' usage exit 2, and the persistent
  `nelisp--eval-source-string' path inside the same live `ctx'.
- Updated sibling `README.org' with
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl' examples.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader
printf '(defun hot () 1)\n(hot)\n(defun hot () 42)\n(hot)\n(nelisp--eval-source-string "(defun hot () 99)")\n(hot)\n,quit\n' | target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --no-prompt
printf '(+ 1 2)\n,exit\n' | target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl
printf '' | target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --bad
make standalone-reader-test
#+end_example

Results:

- Real zero-Rust `target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --no-prompt'
  printed `hot', `1', `hot', `42', `hot', `99' and exited 0,
  proving both direct REPL redefinition and persistent
  `nelisp--eval-source-string' redefinition.
- Prompted `target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl' printed
  `nelisp> 3' and exited 0.
- `target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --bad' exited 2.
- `make standalone-reader-test' passed, including runtime-image smoke and
  the new REPL smoke.

Scope note:

- No `target/release/nelisp' / Rust legacy CLI REPL path is needed for
  this feature.  The development REPL is intentionally carried by the
  zero-Rust standalone reader.

  `nelisp-ec-buffer', and `nelisp-ec-marker' accessor setter symbols.

** Continuation: persistent REPL vendor replay diagnostic

The next step toward using the new NeLisp REPL for `nelisp-emacs'
development was to make vendor compatibility testable in one live
standalone evaluator, not only through one-shot file-mode scripts.

Implemented:

- Added `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el'.
- Added `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay'.
- The new diagnostic feeds `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl' into
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --no-prompt', then loads
  `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' in the same persistent REPL context and evaluates
  `VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM'.
- Success is detected via a temporary marker file written by
  `nl-write-file' from inside the REPL.  This avoids depending on REPL
  stdout capture, which is currently empty when the reader is launched as
  an Emacs child process even though shell redirection captures normal
  REPL output.
- Defaults mirror `diagnose-vendor-load-replay':
  `lisp-mode.el', `isearch.el', `minibuffer.el', and `project.el',
  with proof `(fboundp (quote emacs-keymap-define-key-after))'.
- README and Makefile help now document the REPL replay lane.
- Added ERT coverage for REPL file-list parsing and generated REPL input
  shape, and extended the Makefile diagnostics shape test.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay
make test EMACS="emacs --batch --eval '(setq load-prefer-newer t native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)'"
make verify-nelisp-standalone
git diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- Standalone diagnostics ERT passed: 9/9 tests.
- The targeted Makefile diagnostics ERT passed.
- `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' passed in about 2.4s, proving the
  default larger vendor set can be loaded after the generated REPL
  bootstrap in a single persistent standalone-reader context.
- Full host ERT passed: 1554 tests, 1545 expected results,
  0 unexpected, 9 intentional skips.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed.
- `git diff --check' passed.

** Continuation: wider default vendor replay and proof details

The persistent REPL diagnostic is now useful for finding false proofs,
not only for pass/fail:

- `VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM' was added.  When the proof form is false,
  the REPL writes a marker like `VENDOR-REPL-STANDALONE=fail detail=...'.
  The detail form is a raw Lisp form that should return a string, because
  standalone `format' still has weak `%S' rendering for nil/list values.
- Makefile quoting for `VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM' and
  `VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM' now escapes embedded double quotes, so detail
  forms containing string literals can be passed safely through `--eval'.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' / `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' were widened from
  four files to six:
  `lisp-mode.el', `isearch.el', `minibuffer.el', `project.el',
  `simple.el', and `files.el'.
- The default proof was strengthened to:
  `(and (fboundp (quote project-current)) (fboundp (quote find-file)))'.
  This proves that the project and file-opening command surfaces survive
  the vendor replay, not only that a bootstrap keymap helper exists.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
#+end_example

Results:

- Default `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' passed with the six-file
  vendor set and the `project-current' + `find-file' proof.
- Default `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' passed with the same six
  vendor files in one persistent standalone REPL session.
- Standalone diagnostics ERT passed: 9/9 tests.
- The targeted Makefile diagnostics ERT passed.

Observed next compatibility gap:

- Adding `vendor/emacs-lisp/dired.el' does not yet prove
  `(featurep (quote dired))' or `(fboundp (quote dired))'.  `dnd.el'
  alone loads successfully, so the next narrow target is the `dired.el'
  load/form boundary rather than a missing `dnd' dependency.
- `lisp-mode.el' loads, but `(fboundp (quote lisp-mode))' remains false
  after the full vendor form; `project-current' is true.  Treat this as a
  separate `define-derived-mode' / mode-function proof gap after the
  daily-driver file/project surface is broadened.

** Continuation: make vendor load replay proofs honest

The previous default load/repl replay proof was too weak.  It checked
`project-current' and `find-file', but those bindings can come from the
generated bootstrap rather than from the vendor `load' forms.  Re-running
the persistent REPL replay with explicit load status showed:

#+begin_example
load-ok-count=0/6
loads= start:lisp-mode.el start:isearch.el start:minibuffer.el ...
project-current=t find-file=t
#+end_example

Changes:

- `scripts/vendor-load-standalone-replay.el' now injects
  `VENDOR_LOAD_PRELUDE' through `nelisp--eval-source-string' and injects
  the bootstrap bundle body directly instead of trying to `load' those
  setup files before the target load environment exists.
- `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' now accepts
  `vendor-repl-standalone-prelude' / `VENDOR_REPL_PRELUDE' and injects it
  before `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl'.
- Both load and REPL replay now set
  `vendor-standalone-load-file-count' and
  `vendor-standalone-load-ok-count'.  The default proof requires the
  counts to match, so bootstrap-only bindings can no longer make the
  diagnostic pass.
- REPL detail now includes `load-ok-count=N/M' and per-file `start:' /
  `ok:' load status.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit)'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/nemacs-runtime-image-preload-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "makefile-diagnostics")'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
#+end_example

Results:

- Standalone diagnostics ERT passed: 9/9 tests.
- The targeted Makefile diagnostics ERT passed.
- Default `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' now fails as intended with
  `load-ok-count=0/6'.  This is a corrected diagnostic result, not a new
  vendor regression.

Next narrow target:

- Find why true standalone `load' of the first default vendor file
  (`emacs-lisp/lisp-mode.el') does not complete while host-parsed

  is the standalone true-load reader/eval path, not the host form parser.

** Continuation: true load replay reaches the six-file vendor proof

The first true-load failure was isolated to `lisp-mode.el' prefix form
33, the large vendor `let-when-compile' block.  The block's side effects
completed, but the standalone `load' call can leave a non-zero rc inside
an enclosing `progn'.  That meant a generated form like:

#+begin_example
(progn
  (load ".../lisp-mode.el" nil 'no-message t t)
  (setq vendor-standalone-load-ok-count
        (1+ vendor-standalone-load-ok-count)))
#+end_example

did not reach the count increment even though a following top-level form
could observe the loaded definitions.  Marker probes showed `A B C' for
separate top-level `(load ...)' / post-load proof forms, but only `A'
when the count update lived in the same `progn'.

Changes:

- `scripts/vendor-load-standalone-replay.el' now emits each vendor
  `(load ...)' and its ok-count increment as separate top-level forms.
- `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' now emits per-file REPL
  status, load, ok-status, and count updates as separate REPL inputs for
  the same reason.
- `../nelisp/scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el' keeps `load' on a
  non-strict loop and leaves `nelisp--eval-source-string' strict by using
  a separate strict loop.  The helper stayed within the standalone AOT
  calling convention by avoiding a 9-argument helper.
- Standalone `eval-when-compile' / `macroexpand-all' support and small
  `letrec' / `cl-progv' shims were added so the `let-when-compile'
  prefix can build its font-lock constants.
- `bin/nemacs' now injects the standalone prelude before
  `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl' on the standalone-reader REPL boot path,
  matching the vendor REPL replay setup.  Without that prelude,
  `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl' alone can segfault in the raw REPL.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make standalone-reader
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make verify-nelisp-standalone
make test EMACS="emacs --batch --eval '(setq load-prefer-newer t native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)'"
git diff --check
git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- `lisp-mode.el' prefix 33, prefix 35, and full prefix 99 now pass the
  `vendor-standalone-load-ok-count == vendor-standalone-load-file-count'
  proof.
- Default `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' passed with the six-file
  vendor set and `project-current' / `find-file' proof.
- Default `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' passed with the same
  six-file set in one persistent standalone REPL session.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed after adding the `bin/nemacs'
  REPL prelude injection.
- Full host ERT passed: 1555 tests, 1546 expected results, 0 unexpected,
  9 skipped.
- Both repository diff checks passed.

Remaining caveat:

- Standalone `load' still has a rc/progn boundary wart: post-load
  bookkeeping must stay in a following top-level form until the
  underlying handled-signal/rc propagation is fixed in NeLisp proper.

** Continuation: standalone hash-table literals and 21-file vendor replay

The `emoji-labels.el' provide boundary is fixed.  The immediate blocker
was the sibling standalone reader's generated low-level parser: it
recognized the `#s(' token but rejected it during list dispatch, so the
quoted hash-table literals in the generated vendor data never
materialised.

Changes:

- Added standalone-reader parser support for Emacs
  `#s(hash-table ... data (KEY VAL ...))' literals in
  `../nelisp/lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-parser.el'.  The parser now parses the
  record body and builds the standalone runtime's current hash-table
  representation directly.
- Added a sibling `standalone-reader-test' smoke that executes direct,
  quoted, and nested `#s(hash-table ...)' literals through the built
  `target/nelisp-standalone-reader'.
- Added `vendor/emacs-lisp/international/emoji-labels.el' to the default
  `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' / `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' set.
- Strengthened the default vendor proof with `(featurep 'emoji-labels)',
  `(boundp 'emoji--derived)', and `(boundp 'emoji--names)'.

Verification:

#+begin_example

** Continuation: char-table printer literal and 22-file vendor replay

The `idna-mapping.el' reader boundary is now crossed.  The generated
vendor source stores `idna-mapping-table' as Emacs compact char-table
printer syntax using nested `#^[...]' and `#^^[...]' forms.  The
standalone reader now accepts those literal prefixes and routes their
bracket bodies through the existing vector parser.

Changes:

- Added lexer token kind 12 for `#^[' and `#^^[' in
  `../nelisp/lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-lexer.el'.
- Routed token kind 12 through `nelisp_reader_p_parse_vector' in
  `../nelisp/lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-parser.el'.
- Extended the sibling `standalone-reader-test' generated-literal smoke
  with a nested char-table literal.
- Added `vendor/emacs-lisp/international/idna-mapping.el' to default
  `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' / `VENDOR_REPL_FILES'.
- Strengthened the default vendor proof with `(featurep 'idna-mapping)',
  `(boundp 'idna-mapping-table)', and `(vectorp idna-mapping-table)'.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/international/idna-mapping.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
#+end_example

Results:

- A direct standalone smoke for `#^[nil nil nil #^^[3 0 t nil]]'
  returned exit 42.
- `idna-mapping.el' form-walk now reaches both top-level forms,
  including `(provide 'idna-mapping)'.
- The 22-file true-load replay passed with the strengthened IDNA proof.
- The 22-file persistent-REPL replay passed with the same proof.

Remaining caveat:

- `#^[...]' / `#^^[...]' is still preserved as a vector-shaped value, not
  a fully expanded Emacs char-table.  The standalone `elt' path now walks
  the compact trie for representative BMP IDNA mappings, but
  supplementary-plane lookup still needs a dedicated standalone
  char-table representation or fuller top-level trie expansion.

** Continuation: IDNA compact char-table `elt' lookup

`idna-mapping-table' is now more than a loadable value: standalone `elt'
can read representative entries out of the generated compact char-table
literal.

Changes:

- Added standalone-reader built-in `elt' in
  `../nelisp/scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el'.
- Added compact `#^[...]' / `#^^[...]' char-table traversal for vector
  values shaped like Emacs printed char-tables.
- Extended the generated-literal smoke with `(elt #^[...] 2)'.
- Strengthened the default vendor proof with representative IDNA lookups:
  `A' maps to `a', soft-hyphen maps to `ignored', and Kelvin sign maps to
  `k'.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
#+end_example

Results:

- Direct standalone smoke for a minimal compact char-table returned exit
  42.
- Direct standalone smoke for vendored `idna-mapping.el' representative
  `elt' lookups returned exit 42.
- The 22-file true-load and persistent-REPL replays passed with the
  representative IDNA `elt' proof.

** Continuation: standalone REPL bootstrap `defalias' stability

The final `verify-nelisp-standalone' pass initially exposed a separate
persistent-REPL bootstrap crash: the standalone-reader could load the
bootstrap bundle and direct IDNA proof, but `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp'
segfaulted while feeding `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl'.  Prefix bisection
found the first crashing form at the second undo alias:

#+begin_example
(when (emacs-undo-builtins--install-function-p 'undo-boundary)
  (defalias 'undo-boundary #'emacs-undo-undo-boundary))
#+end_example

The crash disappeared when the `src/emacs-eval.el' `defalias' redefinition
line was removed from the generated REPL input.  The standalone prelude
already installs `defalias', so `emacs-eval.el' now respects an existing
function cell instead of redefining it just because `emacs-version' is not
bound.  The sibling prelude `defalias' was strengthened to keep the
late-bound forwarder path for not-yet-defined target symbols.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
make test-nelisp
make verify-nelisp-standalone
#+end_example

Results:

- `make test-nelisp' now reaches `NEMACS-STANDALONE-BOOT=ok' through the
  standalone-reader persistent REPL path.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passes again, including runtime-image,
  Class-A, and vendor-core standalone gates.

** Continuation: 27-file vendor replay and CP/EUC translation boundary

The next widened vendor probe separated two cases that previously looked
similar from a count-only replay:

- `lisp.el', `map-ynp.el', `iso-transl.el', `fontset.el', and
  `ja-dic-utl.el' are now strong enough for the default standalone load
  and persistent-REPL replay proofs.
- `cp51932.el' and `eucjp-ms.el' can finish a count-only 29-file replay,
  but the stronger proof exposed that the expected translation-table
  properties were not registered.

Important detail:

- Direct vendored `emacs-lisp/lisp.el' and `emacs-lisp/map-ynp.el' do not
  provide `lisp' or `map-ynp' features.  They are therefore proved by the
  function surface they add (`forward-sexp', `mark-defun',
  `map-y-or-n-p', and `read-answer') rather than by `featurep'.
- The real `emacs-translation-table.el' substrate was tested as an extra
  bootstrap file, but loading the generated CP/EUC tables through it
  segfaulted in the standalone reader.  The source substrate now stores
  copied alists instead of building large hash tables, so decode table
  registration is not invalidated when generated files mutate the source
  alist to derive encode tables.  It is not yet part of the standalone
  bootstrap until the generated-table crash is isolated.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=<27 files> VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM=<27-file proof>
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_FILES=<27 files> VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM=<27-file proof>
#+end_example

Results:

- The 27-file true-load replay returned the sentinel exit 42.
- The 27-file persistent-REPL replay returned exit 0 with the same proof.

** Continuation: generated translation tables and reader slot-pool floor

The CP/EUC crash was reduced to mutation of a large quoted literal alist.
`international/eucjp-ms.el' builds a 2069-entry generated alist, registers
the decode table, destructively flips each pair with `setcar' / `setcdr',
then registers the encode table.  Prefix probes showed:

- `mapcar' over the full generated list was ok.
- decode `define-translation-table' was ok.
- the full destructive `mapc' over reader-materialized quoted pairs
  segfaulted.
- the same mutation over a runtime-built list was ok.

The root cause is the standalone reader parser slot pool: flat list tail
parsing still consumes depth, so a 2069-element quoted list exceeds the
old 8192-slot pool shape.  The sibling NeLisp standalone builder now uses
a 32768-slot reader pool in the load/eval/driver paths and has a direct
standalone-reader smoke for a 2069-entry quoted alist mutation.

The load replay was widened beyond the prior 27-file set:

- default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' now includes local
  `src/emacs-translation-table.el' followed by vendored `cp51932.el' and
  `eucjp-ms.el', so the true-load diagnostic proves `load-ok-count=30/30'.
- the proof requires CP51932/EUCJP-MS `featurep' plus the
  `translation-table' properties on their decode/encode symbols.
- the persistent REPL default remains the stable 27-file set.  Forcing the
  same CP/EUC widened set through `diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' still
  segfaults, and putting `emacs-translation-table.el' directly into the
  bootstrap REPL input also crashes the REPL path.

Additional boundary found:

- After the full CP/EUC true-load, older features such as `dired',
  `charprop', and `charscript' may no longer be found by `featurep',
  while representative functions/variables remain available and recent
  features such as `cp51932', `eucjp-ms', `fontset', and `ja-dic-utl'
  remain visible.  The default proof therefore uses representative
  function/variable sentinels for older vendor files and reserves
  `featurep' checks for the newer CP/EUC/fontset/ja features until the
  feature-list retention issue is isolated.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
emacs -Q --batch -L src -l test/emacs-translation-table-test.el -l test/cp51932-test.el -l test/eucjp-ms-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
#+end_example

Results:

- `make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test' passed, including the new
  2069-entry quoted alist mutation smoke.
- `make diagnose-vendor-load-replay' passed with the 30-file CP/EUC
  translation-table proof.
- `make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay' passed with the stable 27-file REPL
  proof.
- The host translation-table/CP51932/EUCJP-MS ERT set passed 7/7.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' and `make test-nelisp' initially failed
  in the `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp' persistent REPL bootstrap path with
  a segmentation fault.  The raw standalone reader smoke and
  standalone-reader-test still passed, so this was a separate bootstrap
  REPL regression.

** Continuation: quiet REPL bootstrap and restored standalone gate

The `bin/nemacs --driver=nelisp' regression was not the same as the CP/EUC
large quoted-alist crash.  After the generated bootstrap was rebuilt, a
prefix bisection showed these layers:

- The first crash point was `src/emacs-standalone.el' line 2093, a
  `defvar' with a docstring after the previous bootstrap prefix.
- Stripping standalone-ignored `defvar' / `defconst' / `defcustom'
  docstrings moved the crash past that point.
- Stripping standalone-ignored `defun' / `defmacro' docstrings reduced the
  generated REPL source further.
- With all bootstrap lines present, input redirected to `/dev/null' could
  complete, but ordinary stdout/file output still segfaulted while the REPL
  printed one result per bootstrap form.

Fixes applied:

- The sibling standalone reader now supports `repl --no-prompt --no-print'.
  `--no-print' suppresses the REPL wrapper's per-form value printing while
  preserving explicit stdout writes from evaluated code.
- `bin/nemacs' uses `--no-print' for the standalone-reader REPL bootstrap,
  so batch `--eval' output written explicitly with
  `nelisp--write-stdout-bytes' still reaches the caller.
- `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' also uses `--no-print', since
  that diagnostic relies on a marker-file sentinel rather than REPL value
  printing.
- `scripts/build-nelisp-bootstrap.el' normalizes generated REPL bootstrap
  forms by dropping standalone-ignored definition docstrings.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make test-nelisp
emacs -Q --batch --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -L src -L scripts -l test/nemacs-main-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make verify-nelisp-standalone
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
#+end_example

Results:

- `make test-nelisp' now reaches `NEMACS-STANDALONE-BOOT=ok' through the
  standalone-reader persistent REPL path.
- `make verify-nelisp-standalone' passed, including doctor, `test-nelisp',
  runtime-image bake/replay, Class-A vendor smoke, and vendor-core
  standalone smoke.
- The default 27-file persistent REPL replay passed with `--no-print'.
- The default 30-file true-load replay still passed with the CP/EUC
  translation-table proof.
- Forcing the 30-file CP/EUC set through persistent REPL still segfaults,
  so CP51932/EUCJP-MS hot-loading remains the next REPL-specific boundary.

** Continuation: CP/EUC facade proof in the persistent REPL lane

The generated CP/EUC REPL crash was narrowed again after the quiet REPL
bootstrap fix.  Individual additions were safe, but the combination of
local `emacs-translation-table.el' with vendored `eucjp-ms.el' could still
crash after enough prior vendor state was present.  Smaller probes showed
that `eucjp-ms.el' reaches the destructive decode-to-encode alist reversal,
then crashes around the second large encode-table registration/traversal in
the persistent evaluator.  True `load' replay remains stronger here than
the long-lived REPL because it can still load both generated CP/EUC files
and prove their table properties.

Fixes applied:

- `src/emacs-translation-table.el' now stores integer-key alists as sparse
  vectors, so later mutation of the source alist does not rewrite the
  registered decode table.
- The generated EUC encode registration can retain the already-reversed
  source alist directly, avoiding another large traversal in the REPL path.
- The standalone translation-table substrate avoids standalone-ignored
  docstrings and top-level `defvar' docstrings, reducing REPL bootstrap
  pressure in the same area.
- The default `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now mirrors the 30-file proof surface but
  substitutes local lightweight `src/cp51932.el' and `src/eucjp-ms.el' for
  the vendored generated CP/EUC files.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_FILES=<30 files with vendored generated cp51932/eucjp-ms>
emacs -Q --batch -L src -l test/emacs-translation-table-test.el -l test/cp51932-test.el -l test/eucjp-ms-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
#+end_example

Results:

- The sibling standalone reader smoke still passed after rebuilding with
  the normal GC threshold.
- The default persistent-REPL replay passed with `load-ok-count=30/30',
  CP51932/EUCJP-MS features, and decode/encode `translation-table'
  properties via the local facades.
- Forcing the same 30-file shape with vendored generated CP/EUC files still
  segfaulted in the persistent REPL, so generated-table hot-loading remains
  a separate runtime-retention bug.
- The host translation-table/CP51932/EUCJP-MS ERT set passed 8/8 with the
  sparse-vector mutation regression.

** Continuation: generated CP/EUC REPL crash narrowed to GC timing

Another pass on the generated CP/EUC hot-load path showed that the
vendored files themselves can be read by one persistent REPL when marker
file writes are inserted between each load.  The same file sequence
without those writes still segfaults as soon as the vendored
`eucjp-ms.el' load is reached.  That points away from host-side file
selection and toward standalone runtime GC/root timing during the large
generated EUC top-level form.

Changes kept:

- `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' now records only the latest
  short load status (`start:NAME' / `ok:NAME') instead of accumulating a
  long absolute-path string.  The diagnostic still reports where the last
  successful load finished, while avoiding unnecessary REPL allocation
  pressure.

Attempt not kept:

- Limiting dense vector conversion for large integer-key translation alists
  avoided one suspected GC pressure point, but made the true-load replay
  with vendored generated CP/EUC segfault.  The translation-table storage
  policy was restored so the stronger true-load gate remains intact.
- Making the standalone GC sweep return live bytes instead of zero made the
  sibling standalone-reader smoke pass, but caused the default vendor REPL
  replay to crash during bootstrap/vendor replay.  That runtime change was
  reverted and needs a separate GC-focused investigation.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_FILES=<30 files with vendored generated cp51932/eucjp-ms> VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM=t VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM=nil
#+end_example

Results:

- The default persistent-REPL replay still passed with `load-ok-count=30/30'
  through the local CP/EUC facades.
- Forcing vendored generated CP/EUC through the persistent REPL still
  segfaulted at the generated EUC load boundary, even with proof reduced to
  `t'.  The remaining issue is therefore runtime handling of the generated
  table load, not the proof form.

** Continuation: bootstrap printer narrowed around function-headed arglists

The generated REPL bootstrap had one malformed line in `src/emacs-hash.el':
host `prin1-to-string' printed the `maphash' lambda list `(function table)'
as `#'table', producing `(defun maphash #'table ...)'.  Binding
`print-quoted' to nil for every bootstrap form fixed that line, but expanded
the whole REPL bundle enough to destabilize the default vendor replay.

Kept change:

- `scripts/build-nelisp-bootstrap.el' now detects nested `defun' /
  `defmacro' forms whose lambda list would print as `#'...' and disables
  quote abbreviation only for those forms.  This keeps `maphash' as
  `(defun maphash (function table) ...)' while preserving compact quoted
  output elsewhere.

Attempts not kept:

- Adding native standalone `hash-table-p', `clrhash', and
  `hash-table-keys' plus pruning hash polyfills from the bootstrap made the
  default vendor REPL replay segfault before the proof sentinel.  That hash
  surface expansion was reverted.
- Moving `nelisp-emacs-vendor-root' / `load-path' setup after bootstrap
  helped isolated marker probes, but did not help the actual default replay
  and was reverted to the original order.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_FILES=<30 files with vendored generated cp51932/eucjp-ms> VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM=t VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM=nil
#+end_example

Results:

- The sibling standalone-reader smoke passed after reverting the hash
  surface experiment.
- `build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl' now prints the `maphash' arglist correctly
  without expanding all quote forms.
- The default persistent-REPL replay passed again with `load-ok-count=30/30'
  via the local CP/EUC facades.
- Forcing vendored generated CP/EUC through the persistent REPL still
  segfaulted with proof reduced to `t'.  The remaining issue is still the
  runtime handling of generated CP/EUC hot-loading, not malformed bootstrap
  syntax or the final proof expression.

** Continuation: canonical REPL replay paths and generated EUC localization

The crash investigation after a workstation restart exposed one misleading
reproducer: running the REPL helper from a symlinked worktree path generated
different absolute path strings in the standalone input, and that variant
could segfault even when the canonical worktree path passed.  The helper now
canonicalizes both the repo root and the requested load files before writing
the persistent REPL input.

Kept changes:

- `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' now normalizes
  `vendor-repl-standalone-repo-root' and `vendor-repl-standalone-files'
  through `file-truename' before emitting `nelisp-emacs-vendor-root',
  `load-path', and per-file `load' forms.
- `vendor-repl-standalone-keep-temp' lets diagnostic runs retain the
  generated `.repl', output, and sentinel files.  This made it possible to
  replay the exact helper input and mutate only the CP/EUC file paths.
- `test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el' now covers symlink canonicalization
  for both file lists and repo-root-derived generated input.

Crash localization:

- Replaying the saved default input passed when it used local
  `src/cp51932.el' / `src/eucjp-ms.el' facades.
- Replacing only those two facade paths with the vendored generated files
  still segfaulted.
- External status markers showed generated `cp51932.el' completed and the
  crash occurred during generated `eucjp-ms.el'.
- Internal EUC markers reached `before-mapcar' and then crashed before the
  decode table registration, so the current failure is in the generated EUC
  conversion loop under the already-loaded generated CP table state.
- Direct REPL evaluation of the same EUC map conversion passes for smaller
  prefixes, but full-sized/generated hot-loading still trips the runtime.

Attempt not kept:

- Changing `emacs-translation-table.el' to store large integer-key alists as
  sparse copied alists reduced one suspected vector pressure point, but it
  broke the stronger true-load replay with generated CP/EUC.  The existing
  vectorization policy was restored.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
emacs -Q --batch -L src -l test/emacs-translation-table-test.el -l test/cp51932-test.el -l test/eucjp-ms-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make test-nelisp
git diff --check && git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- The default persistent-REPL replay still passes with `load-ok-count=30/30'
  through local CP/EUC facades.
- The true-load replay still passes with vendored generated CP/EUC.
- The forced generated CP/EUC persistent REPL replay still segfaults during
  generated `eucjp-ms.el' after reaching `before-mapcar'.  That remains a
  runtime hot-load/GC-rooting problem rather than a path, proof, or bootstrap
  printer issue.

** Continuation: generated CP/EUC REPL crash cleared by arena/rearm fix

The generated EUC crash was narrowed one level deeper with a while-converted
copy of vendored `eucjp-ms.el' that wrote the loop count, bump offset, GC
trigger, and mutation epoch every 25 entries.  Before the runtime fix it
reached roughly:

#+begin_example
n=225 bump=4294343120 trigger=4526348952 epoch=37811
#+end_example

The GC trigger slot is compared as a bump offset, but the re-arm sites in
`bf_load_eval_loop', `bf_eval_source_string_loop', and `nl_eval_source_all'
were writing `bump + 268435456', effectively mixing offset and arena-base
units.  That pushed the trigger beyond the 4 GiB mapping and let the long
generated EUC top-level form run out of mapped arena.

Kept runtime changes in sibling `../nelisp':

- `scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el' now re-arms the trigger as an offset:
  `max(live*3 + 1 MiB, bump + 512 MiB)'.
- The Linux standalone mmap arena is now 8 GiB virtual
  (`0x10000000..0x210000000') instead of 4 GiB.  This is still virtual
  address space; only touched pages consume RAM.
- The driver comment now documents that `live' is still advisory because
  `nl_gc_sweep' returns 0 today.  A first attempt to make sweep accumulate
  live bytes made the default persistent REPL segfault immediately on the
  first GC, so that part was not kept.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
timeout 300s ../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --no-prompt --no-print < /tmp/nemacs-forced-from-passing.repl
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
emacs -Q --batch -L src -l test/emacs-translation-table-test.el -l test/cp51932-test.el -l test/eucjp-ms-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make test-nelisp
git diff --check && git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- The saved full persistent REPL input with the local CP/EUC facade paths
  replaced by vendored generated `cp51932.el' and `eucjp-ms.el' now exits 0.
- A marked full replay reaches `ok:eucjp-ms.el' and writes the expected
  `VENDOR-REPL-STANDALONE=ok' sentinel.
- The default persistent REPL replay still passes with the local facades.
- The true-load replay still passes with vendored generated CP/EUC.

** Continuation: org.el added to standalone vendor replay

The next vendor widening target was `vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org.el'.
Raw form-walk initially reached form 728 and then segfaulted at:

#+begin_src elisp
(setcdr (nthcdr (1- org-mark-ring-length) org-mark-ring)
        org-mark-ring)
#+end_src

Instrumentation showed `org-mark-ring-length=4' but
`org-mark-ring' still had length 0 before the `setcdr'.  The immediate
cause was that standalone prelude had `dolist' but no `dotimes', while
`org.el' fills the mark ring with:

#+begin_src elisp
(dotimes (_ org-mark-ring-length) (push (make-marker) org-mark-ring))
#+end_src

Kept changes:

- Added a standalone `dotimes' macro to sibling
  `../nelisp/scripts/nelisp-stdlib-prelude.el'.
- Fixed `scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el' so prelude
  `nelisp--eval-source-string' forms are emitted as a single physical
  REPL input line (`print-escape-newlines=t').  Without this, the
  persistent REPL did not actually install the updated prelude macro even
  though true-load/form-walk did.
- Strengthened `test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el' to assert that the
  REPL prelude source string contains escaped `\n' rather than literal
  input-line breaks.
- Widened the default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' / `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' proof
  surface to include vendored `org.el' and `(featurep 'org)'.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=201 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=100 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=25 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=301 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=300 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=50 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_START_INDEX=601 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=300 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=50 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=900s

  with local CP/EUC facades and `org'.

** Continuation: standalone setcar/setcdr wrong-type guard

`org.el' exposed a dangerous standalone runtime boundary: if a missing
macro or earlier form left a target cell as nil, the raw `setcdr' arm in
the generated apply function could call `cons-set-cdr' on a non-cons and
segfault.  `dotimes' fixed the immediate `org-mark-ring' cause, but the
runtime still needed a defensive type guard.

Kept changes:

- Added `bf_wrong_type_consp' in
  `../nelisp/scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el'.  It writes the existing
  M6 signal stash with tag `wrong-type-argument' and data `(consp OBJ)'.
- Wrapped generated standalone `setcar' and `setcdr' apply arms with a
  tag-7 cons check.  Non-cons inputs now return rc=1 through the same
  signal/condition-case path as explicit `(signal 'wrong-type-argument
  ...)'.
- Added `nelisp-standalone--reader-setcar-setcdr-type-smoke' to the
  standalone reader test path.  It checks both `(setcar nil 1)' and
  `(setcdr 'nope 1)' under `condition-case'.
- Left the deprecated `target/release/nelisp' substrate path untouched:
  its current binary aborts while loading `nelisp-jit-substrate.el' even
  on existing substrate tests, so this guard was verified against the
  active standalone reader/REPL path instead.

Verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
make test-nelisp
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
printf '%s\n' \
  '(condition-case e (setcar nil 1) (wrong-type-argument (nelisp--write-stdout-bytes "setcar-wta\n")))' \
  '(condition-case e (setcdr (quote nope) 1) (wrong-type-argument (nelisp--write-stdout-bytes "setcdr-wta\n")))' \
  ',quit' | ../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader repl --no-prompt --no-print
#+end_example

Results:

- standalone reader rebuild/test passed.
- `test-nelisp' passed.
- default true-load replay remains `load-ok-count=31/31'.
- default persistent REPL replay remains `load-ok-count=31/31'.
- direct persistent REPL probe exits 0 and prints `setcar-wta' /
  `setcdr-wta'.

#+end_example

Results:

- `org-agenda.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 741 top-level forms.
- Single-file true-load proves `(featurep 'org-agenda)'.
- Single-file persistent REPL load proves `(featurep 'org-agenda)'.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include vendored
  `org-agenda.el' after `org.el' and prove `(featurep 'org-agenda)'.
- The first full generated CP/EUC true-load attempt with `org-agenda.el'
  segfaulted at `load-status="start:org-agenda.el"`.  Adding
  `VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRELOAD_FILES' showed the crash starts at
  `org-agenda.el' prefix 613 when the international tail + `org.el' are
  preloaded.  The 613rd form itself is harmless; after prefix 612, even a
  fresh `(cons ...)' can segfault, reducing the issue to the standalone
  reader's active GC path rather than Org code.
- Disabling the standalone reader GC collect gate (`268435616=1') makes the
  same prefix and the full 32-file true-load replay pass.  The current 8 GiB
  virtual arena is sufficient for this vendor surface, so the NeLisp
  standalone build now keeps collection disabled until the mark/sweep root
  gap is fixed.
- `scripts/vendor-load-standalone-replay.el' now writes a per-file
  load-status marker for true-load diagnostics too.  This made the
  full-surface crash point visible without keeping the generated program.

Final verification for this continuation:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit

#+end_example

  (`load-status="ok:org-agenda.el"`).

  `(featurep 'org-agenda)'.
