** Continuation: org-entities.el added after escaped-symbol and .5 reader support

The next `org-element.el' dependency target was
`vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-entities.el', the Org entity table and lookup
layer.  It has 612 lines and 15 top-level forms.

Two reader/runtime gaps were exposed while walking the raw source:

- Emacs Lisp escaped symbol atoms such as `\"' in the `setminus' entity
  are symbols, not strings.  The sibling standalone reader now handles
  `\X' inside atom scanning by dropping the backslash and admitting the
  escaped byte into the symbol payload.
- Org builds hspace entities with `(format "\\hspace*{%sem}" (* n .5))'.
  Host Emacs accepts leading-dot floats such as `.5', but the standalone
  parser passed `.5' directly to Rust `f64::parse', which rejects it.
  The lexer now normalizes `.5', `-.5', and `+.5' payloads to `0.5',
  `-0.5', and `+0.5' before float parsing while preserving source cursor
  positions.

The standalone reader M5 string/format surface also gained minimal float
emission for the same Org path: `number-to-string', `%s', `%f', and `%g'
can render integer and `.5' fractional float values used by this file.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader /tmp/nelisp-float-direct.el
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-entities.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=120s VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=1
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-entities.el VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-entities)) (fboundp (quote org-entity-get)) (boundp (quote org-entities)))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=120s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-entities.el VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-entities)) (org-entity-get "nbsp"))' VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM='(concat "org-entities=" (if (featurep (quote org-entities)) "t" "nil") " nbsp=" (if (org-entity-get "nbsp") "t" "nil"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=120s
#+end_example

Results:

- Direct standalone reader smokes for `(floatp .5)', `(< .5 1)',
  `(= .5 .5)', `(floatp -.5)', `(number-to-string .5)',
  `(format "%s" .5)', and `(format "%g" .5)' all exit 42.
- `org-entities.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 15 top-level forms.
- Single-file true-load proves `(featurep 'org-entities)',
  `(fboundp 'org-entity-get)', and `(boundp 'org-entities)'
  (`load-status="ok:org-entities.el"`).
- Single-file persistent REPL load proves `(featurep 'org-entities)' and
  `(org-entity-get "nbsp")'.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include vendored
  `org-entities.el' after `org-list.el' and prove
  `(featurep 'org-entities)' plus `(fboundp 'org-entity-get)'.

Final verification for this continuation:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make test-nelisp
git diff --check
git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

** Continuation: org-version.el added before org-macs.el

Following `docs/design/04-small-vendor-foundation-candidates.org', the
next tiny foundation target was `vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-version.el'.
It is the generated 24-line Org version file that defines
`org-release' and `org-git-version'.  It belongs before `org-macs.el'
because `org-macs.el' expands version assertions around `org-release'.

Diagnostics:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-version.el VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-version)) (fboundp (quote org-release)) (fboundp (quote org-git-version)) (stringp (org-release)) (stringp (org-git-version)))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=120s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-version.el VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-version)) (fboundp (quote org-release)) (fboundp (quote org-git-version)) (string= (org-release) "9.7.11") (string= (org-git-version) "release_9.7.11"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=120s
#+end_example

Results:

- Single-file true-load proves `org-version', `org-release',
  `org-git-version', and that both functions return strings.
- Persistent REPL proves the exact `org-release' and `org-git-version'
  strings.
- The standalone true-load proof intentionally uses function/string
  shape plus length in the default proof: constructing the exact expected
  string inside the make-quoted proof form exposed a standalone
  expression mismatch unrelated to loading the vendor file.
- The MCP `nelisp_eval' helper was tried for a small portability probe
  but currently panics even on a simple arithmetic form in this checkout;
  the authoritative checks for this pass remain
  `nelisp-standalone-reader' through the true-load and persistent-REPL
  replay diagnostics.
- `docs/design/04-small-vendor-foundation-candidates.org' now tracks
  candidate status.  `format-spec.el', `org-version.el', `org-macs.el',
  and `org-compat.el' are marked as default replay targets, with
  `org-fold-core.el' left as the next priority target.

make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/ring.el VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote ring)) (fboundp (quote ring-ref)) (let ((r (make-ring 2))) (ring-insert r (quote a)) (ring-insert r (quote b)) (eq (ring-ref r 0) (quote b))))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=120s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/ring.el VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote ring)) (fboundp (quote ring-ref)) (let ((r (make-ring 2))) (ring-insert r (quote a)) (ring-insert r (quote b)) (eq (ring-ref r 0) (quote b))))' VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM='(concat "ring=" (if (featurep (quote ring)) "t" "nil") " ring-ref=" (if (fboundp (quote ring-ref)) "t" "nil"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=120s
#+end_example

Results:

- `ring.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 25 top-level forms.
- Single-file true-load proves `(featurep 'ring)', `(fboundp 'ring-ref)',
  and a minimal `(make-ring 2)' / `ring-insert' / `ring-ref' behavior
  smoke (`load-status="ok:ring.el"`).
- Single-file persistent REPL load proves the same feature/function and
  behavior surface.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include
  vendored `ring.el' after `regi.el' and prove `(featurep 'ring)' plus
  `(fboundp 'ring-ref)'.

** Continuation: generator.el and avl-tree.el added to standalone vendor replay

The next `org-element.el' direct dependency target after `ring.el' was
`vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/avl-tree.el'.  It requires
`generator.el', so the widening was handled as a pair:

- `generator.el': 801 lines, 48 top-level forms, requires `cl-lib'.
- `avl-tree.el': 686 lines, 45 top-level forms, requires `generator'.

This exposed two compatibility gaps in the standalone bootstrap:

- The early `emacs-stub.el' placeholder `cl-defstruct' shadowed the
  richer `emacs-cl-macros.el' shim.  The placeholder is now marked with
  the `emacs-stub-placeholder' property so the later shim can replace it.
- Vendored `avl-tree.el' uses `(:constructor nil)', a second positional
  constructor, `(:predicate avl-tree-p)', and `(:type vector)' nodes
  that are mutated through `setf'.  `emacs-cl-macros.el' now covers that
  subset, and both the local `cl-lib.el' and sibling NeLisp prelude
  `setf' shims understand registered `cl-simple-setter' and
  `cl-struct-setter' properties.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/generator.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/avl-tree.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES='vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/generator.el vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/avl-tree.el' VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote generator)) (featurep (quote avl-tree)) (fboundp (quote avl-tree-create)) (fboundp (quote avl-tree-p)) (let ((tree (avl-tree-create (quote <)))) (avl-tree-enter tree 2) (avl-tree-enter tree 1) (avl-tree-enter tree 3) (and (equal (avl-tree-flatten tree) (quote (1 2 3))) (= (avl-tree-member tree 2) 2))))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES='vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/generator.el vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/avl-tree.el' VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote generator)) (featurep (quote avl-tree)) (fboundp (quote avl-tree-create)) (fboundp (quote avl-tree-p)) (let ((tree (avl-tree-create (quote <)))) (avl-tree-enter tree 2) (avl-tree-enter tree 1) (avl-tree-enter tree 3) (and (equal (avl-tree-flatten tree) (quote (1 2 3))) (= (avl-tree-member tree 2) 2))))' VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM='(concat "generator=" (if (featurep (quote generator)) "t" "nil") " avl-tree=" (if (featurep (quote avl-tree)) "t" "nil") " create=" (if (fboundp (quote avl-tree-create)) "t" "nil"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=300s
#+end_example

Results:

- `generator.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 48 top-level forms.
- `avl-tree.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 45 top-level forms.
- Single-pair true-load proves `generator', `avl-tree',
  `avl-tree-create', `avl-tree-p', `avl-tree-iter', and AVL insert /
  flatten / member behavior.
- Single-pair persistent REPL load proves the same feature/function and
  behavior surface.
- Follow-up resumed `iter-defun' compatibility enough for
  `avl-tree-iter' to become fbound.  The fixes were: standalone
  `lexical-binding' default, Emacs-shaped `macroexp-parse-body',
  minimal `cl-assert', `cl-loop' destructuring plus
  `when ... do ... and collect ...', nested-backquote preservation,
  general macro expansion in `macroexpand-all', and a minimal
  `cl-symbol-macrolet' walker for CPS variable replacement.
- Follow-up fixed the remaining `avl-tree-iter' runtime gap.  The
  standalone `cdr-safe' fallback had been a placeholder returning nil,
  which broke `generator.el' CPS binding extraction, and
  `cl-defstruct' constructor arglists did not lower `&aux' bindings, so
  `avl-tree--stack-create' built an empty iterator stack.  The default
  proof now checks a real iterator smoke by calling `iter-next' three
  times and expecting 1, 2, and 3.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include
  vendored `generator.el' and `avl-tree.el' after `ring.el' and prove
  the same AVL behavior smoke.

Final verification for this continuation:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make test-nelisp
git diff --check
git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

Results:

- Default true-load is green at `load-ok-count=45/45'.
- Default persistent REPL is green at `load-ok-count=45/45'.
- The sibling standalone reader rebuild succeeds.
- Standalone diagnostics ERT is green: 12 tests, 12 expected results.
- `make test-nelisp' is green, including standalone reader smoke and
  `NEMACS-STANDALONE-BOOT=ok'.
- Both repository diffs pass whitespace checks.

** Continuation: AVL iterator runtime proof enabled

The development-machine crash happened after `generator.el' and
`avl-tree.el' were already in the default replay set, but before the
known `avl-tree-iter' runtime gap was closed.  Resuming from the
standalone failure showed two small compatibility misses:

- `car-safe' / `cdr-safe' needed real cons-safe behavior in both the
  nelisp-emacs bootstrap and sibling NeLisp stdlib/prelude.  The nil
  placeholder made `generator.el' lose let-binding init forms during its
  CPS rewrite.
- `cl-defstruct' positional constructor arglists needed to strip `&aux'
  from the generated lambda list and lower aux specs to a surrounding
  `let'.  Vendored `avl-tree.el' uses this shape for
  `avl-tree--stack-create', where the aux `store' value seeds iterator
  state.

The default `VENDOR_AVL_PROOF_FORM' now builds a tree with 2, 1, and 3,
checks flatten/member behavior, creates `(avl-tree-iter tree)', and
requires three `iter-next' calls to return 1, 2, and 3.  Both
`VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM' and `VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM' share that proof,
so true-load and persistent-REPL diagnostics cover the same runtime
iterator path.

Verification for this continuation:

#+begin_example
make -B build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
emacs -Q --batch -L src -L scripts -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el -f ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit
make test-nelisp
git diff --check
git -C ../nelisp diff --check
#+end_example

** Continuation: org-list.el added after reader ## symbol support

The next Org widening target was `vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-list.el',
the plain-list implementation needed by `org-element.el' and practical
Org editing.  It depends on `org-footnote', has 3704 lines and 205
top-level forms.

The first form-walk attempt failed at a `declare-function' hint with an
arglist containing the ordinary Emacs Lisp symbol `##':

#+begin_example
(declare-function org-element-macro-interpreter "org-element" (macro ##))
#+end_example

Host Emacs reads `##' as a symbol, while other unknown `#' dispatches
such as `#foo' remain invalid read syntax.  The sibling standalone reader
therefore gained a narrow `##' sharpsign branch in
`lisp/nelisp-cc-reader-lexer.el', leaving the existing `#'', `#s(',
`#^[' / `#^^[', and radix dispatches unchanged.

Reader verification:

#+begin_example
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader
../nelisp/target/nelisp-standalone-reader /tmp/nelisp-hashhash.el
make -C ../nelisp standalone-reader-test NELISP_SRC='(if (eq (quote ##) (quote ##)) 42 1)'
#+end_example

Results:

- The direct standalone `##' smoke exits 42.
- `standalone-reader-test' passes for
  `(if (eq (quote ##) (quote ##)) 42 1)' and also reports runtime-image
  and REPL smokes passing.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-list.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=25 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES="$(pwd -P)/vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-list.el" VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-list)) (fboundp (quote org-list-to-lisp)))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=600s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES="$(pwd -P)/vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-list.el" VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-list)) (fboundp (quote org-list-to-lisp)))' VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM='(concat "feature=" (if (featurep (quote org-list)) "t" "nil") " to-lisp=" (if (fboundp (quote org-list-to-lisp)) "t" "nil"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=600s
#+end_example

Results:

- `org-list.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 205 top-level forms.
- Single-file true-load proves `(featurep 'org-list)' and
  `(fboundp 'org-list-to-lisp)' (`load-status="ok:org-list.el"`).
- Single-file persistent REPL load proves the same feature/function
  surface.
- Appending `org-list.el' after the default `org-footnote.el' surface
  passes in both true-load and persistent REPL contexts.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include vendored

** Continuation: format-spec.el and org-macs.el added before org-element.el

`org-element.el' remains a large late-stage target: it has 8730 lines,
many parser/cache entry points, and a broad dependency surface.  After a
brief probe, the widening moved back to smaller Org foundation files
that are useful before attempting the full parser.

The selected target pair was:

- `format-spec.el': 205 lines, 5 top-level forms, required by
  `org-macs.el'.
- `org-macs.el': 1821 lines, 151 top-level forms, the Org macro and
  utility layer used by later Org components.

#+end_example

** Continuation: org-fold-core.el added as the fold foundation

broad dependency surface.  The next small foundation target was

including `org-fold-core-add-folding-spec',

** Continuation: oc.el added to the default vendor replay

The next candidate from

load-time requires are still small: `org-macs', `org-compat', and `seq'

limited to load and citation registry surface; parser/export runtime
behavior remains deferred until the broader Org element stack is ready.

`org-cycle-global', `org-cycle-overview', `org-cycle-content',
`org-cycle-hide-drawers', `org-cycle-force-archived',
`org-cycle-hook', `org-cycle-global-status', and
`org-cycle-subtree-status'.  Direct load-time requires are `org-macs'
and `org-fold' (`org-macs' appears twice in the source); references to
`org-element', `org-list', `org-table', and other Org layers are only
declarations here.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-cycle.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=25 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=600s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES='vendor/emacs-lisp/format-spec.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-version.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-macs.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-compat.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-fold-core.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-fold.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-cycle.el' VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-cycle)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-global)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-overview)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-content)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-hide-drawers)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-force-archived)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-hook)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-global-status)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-subtree-status)))' VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES='vendor/emacs-lisp/format-spec.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-version.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-macs.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-compat.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-fold-core.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-fold.el vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org-cycle.el' VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM='(and (= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count) (featurep (quote org-cycle)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-global)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-overview)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-content)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-hide-drawers)) (fboundp (quote org-cycle-force-archived)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-hook)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-global-status)) (boundp (quote org-cycle-subtree-status)))' VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM='(concat "org-cycle=" (if (featurep (quote org-cycle)) "t" "nil") " cycle=" (if (fboundp (quote org-cycle)) "t" "nil") " global=" (if (fboundp (quote org-cycle-global)) "t" "nil") " hook=" (if (boundp (quote org-cycle-hook)) "t" "nil"))' VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=300s
#+end_example

Results:

- `org-cycle.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 88 top-level forms.
- Single-stack true-load proves `org-cycle', `org-cycle-global',
  `org-cycle-overview', `org-cycle-content',
  `org-cycle-hide-drawers', `org-cycle-force-archived',
  `org-cycle-hook', `org-cycle-global-status', and
  `org-cycle-subtree-status' (`load-status="ok:org-cycle.el"`).
- Single-stack persistent REPL load proves the same feature/function and
  variable surface.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include
  vendored `org-cycle.el' after `org-keys.el'.

Final verification for this continuation:

** Continuation: tempo.el and org-tempo.el added to the default vendor replay

The next candidate after `org-cycle.el' was

ASCII case, mirroring, and special casing, but the standalone proof-time
environment does not currently expose `char-code-property-alist',
`define-char-code-property', or `get-char-code-property'.  A runtime
lookup proof therefore remains deferred until that char-property surface
is visible in NeLisp.

Larger Unicode generated files remain deferred:

- `uni-bidi.el' reaches a single `define-char-code-property' form and
  exits 84.
- `uni-category.el' fails in the general-category table path with exit
  88.
- `uni-confusable.el' segfaults while evaluating the first giant
  `defconst'.
- `uni-brackets.el', `uni-combining.el', `uni-comment.el', and
  `uni-decomposition.el' contain generated binary/NUL table payloads and
  fail standalone form-walk.

** Continuation: small loaddefs/autoload files added

Following the June 3 direction, `org-element.el' remains deferred until a
late Org parser pass.  `thai-util.el' also remains deferred for the Thai
word-boundary pass because it directly requires the much larger
`thai-word.el'.  This pass instead selected eight small loaddefs/autoload
registration files with no direct `require' forms:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/calendar/holiday-loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/cedet/ede/loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/theme-loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/eshell/esh-module-loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/cedet/srecode/loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/calendar/diary-loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/textmodes/texinfo-loaddefs.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/calc/calc-loaddefs.el'

The EDE and SRecode loaddefs files both provide the feature `loaddefs',
so proof forms intentionally avoid treating that feature as unique.  The
standalone runtime also does not currently materialize these autoload
forms as ordinary `fboundp' function cells, so the stable proof uses file
count, provided features, and SRecode's `global-srecode-minor-mode'
variable surface.

Standalone probes:

** Continuation: iso8601.el and parse-time.el added to the default vendor replay

The next non-Org foundation candidate after `time-date.el' was
`vendor/emacs-lisp/calendar/parse-time.el'.  It directly requires
`iso8601', so this continuation widened the default stack by adding
`vendor/emacs-lisp/calendar/iso8601.el' first and then
`parse-time.el'.  The `anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline reported 30
definitions in `iso8601.el', including `iso8601-parse',
`iso8601-parse-date', `iso8601-parse-time', `iso8601-parse-zone',
`iso8601-valid-p', `iso8601-parse-duration', and
`iso8601-parse-interval'.  It reported 10 definitions in `parse-time.el',
including `parse-time-tokenize', `parse-time-string',
`parse-iso8601-time-string', and the month/weekday/zone tables.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/calendar/parse-time.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s

Results:

- `parse-time.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 14 top-level forms.
- `iso8601.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 33 top-level forms.
- Single-file true-load and persistent REPL prove `iso8601' on top of
  `time-date.el' with representative ISO parser function and regexp
  table surface (`load-status="ok:iso8601.el"`).
- Loading `parse-time.el' by itself reaches `provide', but
  `parse-time-rules' is not bound after standalone replay.  Loading
  `time-date.el', `iso8601.el', and `parse-time.el' together still leaves
  `parse-time-rules' unbound, so the default proof intentionally covers
  the feature/function surface plus the month/weekday/zone tables and
  leaves RFC-style fallback parsing as a follow-up.
- Appending `iso8601.el' and `parse-time.el' to the default true-load and
  persistent REPL stacks proves the same load surface.
- Default `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include
  vendored `iso8601.el' and `parse-time.el' after `time-date.el'.  The
  default proof and REPL detail surface also require/report `iso8601' and
  `parse-time'.
- The candidate queue now marks both files as default replay and keeps
  `org-element.el' deferred.  The remaining small calendar files require
  the larger `calendar.el' core, so they stay in the defer bucket.

#+end_example

  `load-status="ok:parse-time.el"'.

  `iso8601=t' and `parse-time=t' in the detail surface.

** Continuation: ol-man.el, ol-rmail.el, ol-mhe.el, ol-w3m.el, and ol-irc.el added

** Continuation: let-alist.el, radix-tree.el, text-property-search.el, and thunk.el added

After the small Org link modules, the candidate queue had no remaining
unadopted "Next" entries, so this pass scanned small unadopted vendor
files under the Org, calendar, emacs-lisp, and textmodes directories.
It kept `org-element.el' deferred and selected four general
emacs-lisp foundations that do not pull broad UI/parser surfaces:
`let-alist.el', `radix-tree.el', `text-property-search.el', and
`thunk.el'.

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outlines used for the selected files:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/let-alist.el' is 165 lines and exposes
  `let-alist--deep-dot-search', `let-alist--access-sexp',
  `let-alist--list-to-sexp', `let-alist--remove-dot', and
  `let-alist'.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/radix-tree.el' is 250 lines and exposes
  the internal insert/remove/lookup walkers, `radix-tree-empty',
  `radix-tree-insert', `radix-tree-lookup', `radix-tree-subtree',
  `radix-tree-prefixes', `radix-tree-iter-subtrees',
  `radix-tree-iter-mappings', `radix-tree-count', and
  `radix-tree-from-map'.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/text-property-search.el' is 236 lines
  and exposes forward/backward text property search plus the generated
  `prop-match' accessors.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/thunk.el' is 132 lines, requires
  `cl-lib', and exposes `thunk-delay', `thunk-force',
  `thunk-evaluated-p', `thunk-let', and `thunk-let*'.

** Continuation: rmc.el, generate-lisp-file.el, obarray.el, soundex.el, cursor-sensor.el, indent-aux.el, and display-fill-column-indicator.el added

After moving the first batch of general emacs-lisp foundations into the
default replay, this pass scanned the remaining small unadopted vendor
files and kept `org-element.el' deferred.  It selected seven shallow
utility/display helper files: `rmc.el', `generate-lisp-file.el',
`obarray.el', `soundex.el', `cursor-sensor.el', `indent-aux.el', and
`display-fill-column-indicator.el'.  `float-sup.el' was tested but
deferred because standalone form-walk reaches 6/10 forms and then exits
with a floating point exception in the float-limit `defconst' area.

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outlines used for the selected files:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/rmc.el' is 312 lines and exposes
  `rmc--add-key-description', `rmc--show-help',
  `read-multiple-choice', and the short/long answer helpers.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/generate-lisp-file.el' is 119 lines and
  exposes `generate-lisp-file-heading' and
  `generate-lisp-file-trailer'.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/cursor-sensor.el' is 227 lines and
  exposes `cursor-sensor-inhibit', tangible-position helpers, and
  cursor detection helpers.  It also contains minor-mode definitions,
  but those generated mode entry points are not part of the default
  proof yet.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/obarray.el' is 59 lines and exposes the small
  obarray helper API.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/soundex.el' is 65 lines and exposes `soundex'.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/indent-aux.el' is 76 lines and exposes
  `kill-ring-deindent-buffer-substring-function' plus a minor-mode
  definition.
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/display-fill-column-indicator.el' is 87 lines and
  exposes `display-fill-column-indicator--turn-on' plus a minor-mode
  definition.

** Continuation: tabify/rot13/widget/mail/HMAC small utility batch added

After the Unicode case/mirroring data pass, the candidate queue had no
remaining non-deferred entries, so this pass scanned the vendored tree
for additional small, low-dependency files that were not yet recorded in
`docs/design/04-small-vendor-foundation-candidates.org'.  It kept
terminal, language, URL, and larger subsystem files out of the default
lane for now, and selected a utility/mail/HMAC batch:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/tabify.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/rot13.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/textmodes/underline.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/widget.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/dos-vars.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mb-depth.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/ietf-drums.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc2045.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-def.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-md5.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/rfc2104.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before widening the
default replay:

- `tabify.el' exposes `untabify', `tabify-regexp', and `tabify'.
- `rot13.el' exposes `rot13-display-table', `rot13-translate-table',
  `rot13', `rot13-string', `rot13-region', `rot13-other-window', and
  `toggle-rot13-mode'.
- `underline.el' exposes `underline-region' and `ununderline-region'.
- `widget.el' is a small compatibility wrapper exposing
  `define-widget-keywords' and `define-widget'.
- `mb-depth.el' exposes `minibuffer-depth-indicator-function',
  `minibuffer-depth-indicator', `minibuffer-depth-overlay', and
  `minibuffer-depth-setup'.  Its generated minor-mode command is not
  part of the default proof yet.
- `rfc2045.el' exposes `rfc2045-encode-string' and requires
  `ietf-drums'.
- `ietf-drums.el' exposes the RFC token tables and address/header
  parsing helpers.
- `hmac-def.el' exposes `define-hmac-function'.
- `hmac-md5.el' exposes `md5-binary', `hmac-md5', and `hmac-md5-96',
  after `hmac-def' plus the already-loaded `hex-util' and built-in `md5'
  surface.
- `rfc2104.el' exposes `rfc2104-hash'.

Verification before widening the default surface:

** Continuation: compat.el, shorthands.el, dynamic-setting.el, and Unicode numeric data added

Following the decision to leave `org-element.el' until later, this pass
continued widening smaller non-Org foundations.  It selected three
compact helper files plus three generated Unicode numeric property files:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/compat.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/shorthands.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/dynamic-setting.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/international/uni-decimal.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/international/uni-digit.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/international/uni-numeric.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before widening the
default replay:

- `compat.el' exposes the compatibility macros `compat-function' and
  `compat-call'.
- `shorthands.el' exposes `hack-read-symbol-shorthands',
  `elisp-shorthand-font-lock-face', and
  `shorthands-font-lock-shorthands'.  It intentionally has no `provide'
  surface, so replay proof uses function/face symbols instead.
- `dynamic-setting.el' exposes `font-use-system-font',
  `font-setting-change-default-font', and
  `dynamic-setting-handle-config-changed-event'.
- `uni-decimal.el', `uni-digit.el', and `uni-numeric.el' are generated
  `define-char-code-property' data files with no ordinary function
  definitions.

Verification before widening the default surface:

  exit 88.

  through `load-status="ok:uni-numeric.el"'.
- The six-file persistent REPL probe proves the same surface and reports
  `extra-foundations=compat/shorthands/dynamic-setting
  unicode-numeric=load-only'.

  `compat.el', `shorthands.el', `dynamic-setting.el', `uni-decimal.el',
  `uni-digit.el', and `uni-numeric.el' after the previous
  utility/mail/HMAC files.
- The default true-load replay is green at `load-ok-count=108/108' and
  ends with `load-status="ok:uni-numeric.el"'.
- The default persistent REPL replay is green at `load-ok-count=108/108'
  and appends
  `extra-foundations=compat/shorthands/dynamic-setting
  unicode-numeric=load-only' to the detail surface.

** Continuation: benchmark/password/interaction helpers added

With `org-element.el' still deferred, this pass scanned unadopted small
vendored files and selected six compact helper files that do not pull
large parser, URL, terminal, language, or CEDET surfaces:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/benchmark.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/password-cache.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/double.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/chistory.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/scroll-lock.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/thread.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before widening the
default replay:

- `benchmark.el' exposes `benchmark-elapse', `benchmark-call',
  `benchmark-run', `benchmark-run-compiled', `benchmark', and
  `benchmark-progn'.
- `password-cache.el' exposes cache customization variables plus
  `password-read-from-cache', `password-in-cache-p', `password-read',
  `password-cache-remove', `password-cache-add', and `password-reset'.
- `double.el' exposes `double-map', `double-prefix-only',
  `double-read-event', and `double-translate-key', and requires
  `isearch'.
- `chistory.el' exposes command-history listing/repeat helpers and a
  `command-history-mode' derived from `special-mode'.
- `scroll-lock.el' exposes scroll-lock movement helpers and a minor-mode
  keymap surface.
- `thread.el' requires `backtrace' and exposes thread list/status/signal
  helpers on top of tabulated-list mode surface.

Verification before widening the default surface:

** Continuation: mail encoder and transaction queue helpers added

Following the decision to leave `org-element.el' until a later parser
pass, this pass scanned another group of compact non-Org helper files and
selected six that have shallow load surfaces:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/qp.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/mailheader.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/yenc.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/flow-fill.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/uudecode.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/tq.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before widening the
default replay:

- `qp.el' exposes `quoted-printable-decode-region',
  `quoted-printable-decode-string', `quoted-printable-encode-region',
  and `quoted-printable-encode-string'.
- `mailheader.el' exposes header extraction, parse, set, merge, and
  format helpers.
- `yenc.el' exposes part checks, region decoding, filename extraction,
  and line parsing.
- `flow-fill.el' exposes flowed text encode/fill helpers plus test data.
- `uudecode.el' exposes internal and external decoder paths; the default
  proof only checks load/function surface and does not execute the
  external decoder.
- `tq.el' exposes transaction queue accessors, enqueue/close/filter, and
  process-buffer helpers; the default proof does not require a live
  process.

Verification before widening the default surface:

** Continuation: MIME mail parsing helpers added

Following the June 3 direction, `org-element.el' remains deferred until a
later parser/dependency pass.  This pass instead widened the non-Org
mail/MIME foundation surface with six helper files that form-walk and
load cleanly:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/mail-prsvr.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/gnus/mm-util.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc2047.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc2231.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/mail-parse.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc6068.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before promotion:

- `mail-prsvr.el' only defines the mail charset preserve variables.
- `mm-util.el' exposes MIME charset, coding-system, file, buffer, and
  image/decompression helper surface and requires `mail-prsvr' plus
  `timer'.
- `rfc2047.el' exposes MIME encoded-word encode/decode helpers and sits
  on `mm-util', `ietf-drums', `mail-prsvr', and `rfc2045'.
- `rfc2231.el' exposes MIME parameter decode/encode helpers and sits on
  `ietf-drums' and `rfc2047'.
- `mail-parse.el' mostly provides compatibility aliases across
  `mail-prsvr', `ietf-drums', `rfc2231', `rfc2047', and `rfc2045'.
- `rfc6068.el' exposes `rfc6068-unhexify-string' and
  `rfc6068-parse-mailto-url'.

Two nearby files remain deferred:

- `blessmail.el' is an install-time generator with top-level file writes
  and `kill-emacs', so it is not suitable for replay.
- `rmailmsc.el' requires `rmail' directly and should wait for a broader
  Rmail surface pass.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/mail-prsvr.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc6068.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc2231.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/gnus/mm-util.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/rfc2047.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/mail/mail-parse.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES="<six MIME mail helper files>" VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM="<MIME mail helper proof>" VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s

#+end_example

Results:

- `mail-prsvr.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 4 top-level forms.

- A first `rfc6068-parse-mailto-url' runtime smoke was not promoted: the
  file load itself reached `ok:rfc6068.el', but the runtime expectation
  failed.  The default proof therefore stays at feature/function surface.
- The six-file true-load probe proves load count equality plus
  feature/function surface through `load-status="ok:rfc6068.el"'.
- The six-file persistent REPL probe proves the same surface and reports
  `mime-mail-helpers=mail-prsvr/mm-util/rfc2047/rfc2231/mail-parse/rfc6068'.

Default replay changes:

- `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include
  `mail-prsvr.el', `mm-util.el', `rfc2047.el', `rfc2231.el',
  `mail-parse.el', and `rfc6068.el' after the mail encoder/header and
  transaction queue helpers.
- The default true-load replay is green at `load-ok-count=126/126' and
  ends with `load-status="ok:rfc6068.el"'.
- The default persistent REPL replay is green at `load-ok-count=126/126'
  and appends
  `mime-mail-helpers=mail-prsvr/mm-util/rfc2047/rfc2231/mail-parse/rfc6068'
  to the detail surface.

** Continuation: SASL helper surface added to the default vendor replay

With `org-element.el' still deferred for a later parser/dependency pass,
this pass selected the small SASL authentication helper files after the
mail utility surface:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-cram.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-digest.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-scram-rfc.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-scram-sha256.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before promotion:

- `sasl.el' exposes the core SASL client/mechanism helpers plus the
  built-in PLAIN, LOGIN, and ANONYMOUS mechanism surfaces.
- `sasl-cram.el' adds the CRAM-MD5 response helper on top of `sasl' and
  the already-promoted `hmac-md5'.
- `sasl-digest.el' adds the DIGEST-MD5 parser/response helpers on top
  of `sasl' and `hmac-md5'.
- `sasl-scram-rfc.el' adds SCRAM RFC helper functions and provides both
  `sasl-scram-rfc' and `sasl-scram-sha-1'.
- `sasl-scram-sha256.el' adds the SCRAM-SHA-256 helper surface on top
  of `sasl-scram-rfc' and the already-promoted `rfc2104'.
- `sasl-ntlm.el' was left deferred because it directly requires
  `ntlm.el'.

Verification before widening the default surface:

** Continuation: MD4, NTLM, and SASL-NTLM added to the default vendor replay

With `org-element.el' still deferred, this pass returned to the
previously deferred NTLM side of the SASL surface:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/md4.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/ntlm.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-ntlm.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before promotion:

- `md4.el' exposes the pure Lisp `md4' implementation plus pack/unpack
  helpers.
- `ntlm.el' exposes NTLM request/response generation, password hash
  helpers, and the DES-style SMB hash support.  It requires `md4' and
  the already-promoted `hmac-md5'.
- `sasl-ntlm.el' is a thin SASL adapter on top of `sasl' and `ntlm',
  exposing `sasl-ntlm-request' and `sasl-ntlm-response'.

Verification before widening the default surface:

#+begin_example
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/md4.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/net/ntlm.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRELOAD_FILES="vendor/emacs-lisp/md4.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-def.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-md5.el" VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl-ntlm.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRELOAD_FILES="vendor/emacs-lisp/md4.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-def.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/hmac-md5.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/sasl.el vendor/emacs-lisp/net/ntlm.el" VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=5 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_TIMEOUT=300s
make diagnose-vendor-load-replay VENDOR_LOAD_FILES="<md4/ntlm/sasl-ntlm files>" VENDOR_LOAD_PROOF_FORM="<NTLM proof>" VENDOR_LOAD_TIMEOUT=900s
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_FILES="<md4/ntlm/sasl-ntlm files>" VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM="<NTLM proof>" VENDOR_REPL_DETAIL_FORM="<NTLM detail>" VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s
#+end_example

Results:

- `md4.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 18 top-level forms.
- `ntlm.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 34 top-level forms.
- `sasl-ntlm.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 7 top-level forms.
- The three-file true-load probe proves load count equality, the
  `md4', `ntlm', and `sasl-ntlm' features, representative function
  surface, a 16-byte `md4' runtime smoke, and a 36-byte
  `ntlm-build-auth-request' runtime smoke through
  `load-status="ok:sasl-ntlm.el"'.
- The three-file persistent REPL probe proves the same surface and
  reports `ntlm-helpers=md4/ntlm/sasl-ntlm/load-ok-count=3/3'.
- A narrower probe showed that `(get 'sasl-ntlm 'sasl-mechanism)' is not
  a stable standalone proof yet, so the default proof intentionally uses
  the adapter's feature/function surface rather than that property.

Default replay changes:

- `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include `md4.el',
  `ntlm.el', and `sasl-ntlm.el'.
- The default proof covers feature/function surface plus the small MD4
  and NTLM request length smokes.  Live NTLM/SASL authentication
  exchanges remain follow-ups.
- The candidate queue records all three as `default replay' and removes
  the old `sasl-ntlm.el' defer entry.

Final verification after adding the three files to the default replay:

make test-nelisp
#+end_example

** Continuation: version, help-macro, env, and fileloop helpers added

With `org-element.el' still deferred because of its dependency surface,
this pass picked four smaller core helper files:

- `vendor/emacs-lisp/version.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/help-macro.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/env.el'
- `vendor/emacs-lisp/fileloop.el'

`anvil.el' / emacs-eval outline inspection was used before promotion:

- `version.el' exposes version constants plus `emacs-version',
  `emacs-repository-get-version', and `emacs-repository-get-branch'.  It
  has no `provide' form.
- `help-macro.el' requires `backquote' and exposes the help-screen macro
  surface around `make-help-screen' and `help--help-screen'.
- `env.el' exposes environment helper APIs such as
  `substitute-env-vars', `substitute-env-in-file-name', `setenv', and
  `getenv'.
- `fileloop.el' requires the already-promoted `generator' and exposes
  the multi-file scan/replace helper surface.

- `version.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 24 top-level forms.

- `env.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 11 top-level forms.
- `fileloop.el' standalone form-walk reaches all 15 top-level forms
  with `generator.el' preloaded.
- The four-file true-load probe proves load count equality, version
  variables/function surface, the `help-macro', `env', and `fileloop'
  features, and representative helper function surface through
  `load-status="ok:fileloop.el"'.
- The four-file persistent REPL probe proves the same surface and
  reports `core-helpers=version/help-macro/env/fileloop/load-ok-count=4/4'.
- Narrower runtime probes showed that calling `emacs-version' and the
  `setenv' / `substitute-env-vars' smoke do not return to the standalone
  REPL sentinel yet, so the default proof intentionally stays at load
  and helper API surface for these files.

Default replay changes:

- `VENDOR_LOAD_FILES' and `VENDOR_REPL_FILES' now include `version.el',
  `help-macro.el', `env.el', and `fileloop.el'.

  `help-macro', `env', and `fileloop' feature/function surface.

  `core-helpers=version/help-macro/env/fileloop'.
- The candidate queue records all four as `default replay'.

for those files is the replay load-count and final load status rather

Terminal files around `xterm.el', URL transport helpers that require
`url-parse.el', Quail input methods, and CEDET/Gnus/MH/EPA/Org-Babel/Eshell
surfaces were left out of this batch.

The MCP `nelisp_eval' path was checked but cannot direct-load these files yet:
calling `(load ...)' returns `(nelisp-void-function load)'.  The anvil
definitions index also did not cover vendored symbols such as
`ansi-osc-filter-region' or `textsec-suspicious-p', so the authoritative proof
remained the standalone replay scripts.

`netrc-get', and `netrc-machine-user-or-password'.  The proof-form-local

does not return through the expected sentinel.  Separate pre-created-file
probes also leave `netrc-credentials' over a temporary `netrc-file' and
synthetic `netrc-services-file' lookup through `netrc-find-service-name' /
numeric `netrc-port-equal' unpromoted; true-load exits with `exit=13' for
those paths and the REPL returns a fail sentinel with `load-ok-count=1/1'.

This pass therefore still does not claim GPG cache handling, `/etc/services'
behavior, or the file-IO path inside `netrc-credentials'.

Adding `netrc.el' to the current accumulated default persistent REPL set is
still not safe: default `253/253' plus `netrc.el' constructs a 254-file probe
and segfaults before producing a sentinel.

No Makefile replay list changed in this pass.  The default true-load path
therefore remains `319/319', and the default persistent REPL path remains
`253/253'.  The candidate queue keeps `netrc.el' as default true-load only
with full REPL deferred.

therefore not promoted to standalone.

the file load succeeds and that `featurep 'cyril-jis' remains nil, matching the
absence of a `provide' form.

`quail-package-alist', or `quail-current-package' as stable post-load clauses,
so this pass does not claim package registration for `cyrillic-jis-russian',
live input-method activation, or rule lookup behavior.

Adding `cyril-jis.el' to the current accumulated default persistent REPL set is
still not safe: default `253/253' plus `cyril-jis.el' constructs a 254-file
probe and segfaults before producing a sentinel.

** Continuation: mixed mail URL and terminal integration files remain deferred

This pass continued through the next Defer rows after the Org link modules:

- `rmailmsc.el': standalone form-walk reaches 2/2 forms; isolated true-load and

  proof for `gpm-mouse-mode' and `gpm-mouse-enable' fails with a fail sentinel,

** Continuation: float-sup FPE narrowed to atan-derived denominator

`org-element.el' remains deferred near the end of the Org foundation pass.
After moving `blessmail.el' out of the replay queue, this pass returned to the
smallest real runtime blocker still in Defer:
`vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/float-sup.el'.

MCP `nelisp_eval' for a direct `(/ 180.0 3.141592653589793)' probe returned
`Transport closed', so the runtime checks used the local standalone-reader
diagnostic path.

Current `float-sup.el' source and diagnostic evidence:

- `float-sup.el' is 55 lines and has no direct `require' forms.
- It defines `float-pi' as `(* 4 (atan 1))', then
  `degrees-to-radians' as `(/ float-pi 180.0)' and `radians-to-degrees' as
  `(/ 180.0 float-pi)'.
- The current full form-walk still reads 10 forms and evaluates 6 before index
  7, the `radians-to-degrees' `defconst', exits with
  `"Floating point exception"'.
- A minimal standalone form-walk probe with
  `(defconst literal-pi 3.141592653589793)' followed by
  `(defconst literal-div (/ 180.0 literal-pi))' passes both forms.
- The same probe defines `(defconst atan-pi (* 4 (atan 1)))' successfully, but
  `(defconst atan-div (/ 180.0 atan-pi))' fails with
  `"Floating point exception"'.
- A second probe confirms `(defconst atan1 (atan 1))',
  `(defconst atan1-plus (+ 0.0 atan1))', and
  `(defconst atan1-mul (* 4 atan1))' pass, then
  `(defconst atan1-lit-div (/ 180.0 atan1))' fails with
  `"Floating point exception"'.

The blocker is therefore narrower than generic float literal division:
`atan'-derived float values can flow through `+' and `*', but using such a
value as the denominator of `/` through the current `nl_jit_float_div' path can
raise SIGFPE.  No runtime code changed in this pass.  The candidate queue keeps
`float-sup.el' in Defer with the more specific `atan' denominator / float
division blocker recorded.

** Continuation: float-sup FPE narrowed to default built-in slash

`org-element.el' remains deferred near the end of the Org foundation pass.
This pass continued the `float-sup.el' diagnosis without adding it to either

MCP `nelisp_eval' for `(/ 180.0 (atan 1))' returned `Transport closed', so the
runtime checks again used local standalone-reader diagnostics.

Additional probe evidence:

- A direct `nl_jit_float_div' call with an `(atan 1)'-derived denominator
  passes.

  `/` also passes.

  `../nelisp/lisp/nelisp-stdlib.el' after bootstrap makes the minimal
  `(/ 180.0 atan1)' probe pass.

  `VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRELOAD_FILES' lets full `float-sup.el' form-walk reach

the standalone-reader built-in `/` present in the default bootstrap path.  The
candidate queue keeps `float-sup.el' in Defer because default replay must pass
without the temporary source-level override.

- Field-key progression and return-key buffer mutation are not promoted yet.
  Persistent-REPL probes around `bib-find-key' and `bib-return-key' do not
  return to the proof sentinel.
- The file is already in the default true-load list and remains excluded from
  the default persistent REPL list.
- Adding `bib-mode.el' as the 254th accumulated persistent-REPL file still
  segfaults before sentinel.
- Obsolete variable-alias parity, command metadata, stable live mode state
  beyond `major-mode', field-key progression, title capitalization,
  unread-file append behavior, and accumulated persistent REPL adoption remain
  deferred.

No Makefile replay list changed in this pass.  `bib-mode.el' remains
default-true-load-only, with detailed proof stable in isolated load/REPL for

- Command metadata is still a standalone boundary: `reveal-hide-revealed' and
  `reveal-post-command' are not `commandp' in isolated true-load or

  `buffer-modified-tick' are not `fboundp' in isolated true-load or
  persistent REPL.

** Continuation: emacs-lock true-load-only boundary rechecked

`org-element.el' and Babel-facing `ob.el' remain deferred until late because
their dependency surfaces are broader than the small default candidates
selected for this pass.  This pass moved from `reveal.el' to
`vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lock.el', a 250-line locked-buffer guard helper.

Anvil `file_outline' and `nelisp_eval' returned `Transport closed', so the
outline and replay checks used local file reads plus standalone-reader
diagnostics.

Current `emacs-lock.el' evidence:

- The file has no direct runtime `require'.  Its top-level surface includes
  the `emacs-lock' group, `emacs-lock-default-locking-mode',
  `emacs-lock-unlockable-modes', `emacs-lock-locked-buffer-functions',
  permanent-local `emacs-lock-mode', `emacs-lock--old-mode', and
  `emacs-lock--try-unlocking', `emacs-lock-live-process-p',
  `emacs-lock--can-auto-unlock', `emacs-lock--exit-locked-buffer',
  `emacs-lock--kill-emacs-hook',
  `emacs-lock--kill-emacs-query-functions',
  `emacs-lock--kill-buffer-query-functions', `emacs-lock--set-mode', the
  source `define-minor-mode' for `emacs-lock-mode', noninteractive-gated
  kill hooks, `emacs-lock-unload-function', and `(provide 'emacs-lock)'.
- Standalone form-walk reaches all 21 top-level forms.
- Native Emacs loads the file with the `emacs-lock' feature, all eight helper
  functions, generated `emacs-lock-mode' as a command,
  `emacs-lock-unload-function', Custom defaults, permanent-local state
  variables, direct setter behavior, direct `emacs-lock-mode' activation, and
  a kill-locked `emacs-lock--kill-buffer-query-functions' smoke returning nil.
- Isolated true-load over only `emacs-lock.el' exits 42 with
  `load-status="ok:emacs-lock.el"' when the proof checks count 1, the
  `emacs-lock' feature, all helper/minor-mode/unload function bindings, the
  Custom variables, and the buffer-local state variables.
- Isolated persistent REPL over only `emacs-lock.el' exits 0 with the same
  count/feature/function/variable proof.
- Current process/hook/prompt primitives are present in isolated true-load and
  persistent REPL: `process-live-p', `get-buffer-process',
  `run-hook-with-args', `y-or-n-p', and `kill-local-variable' are all
  `fboundp'.
- Setter behavior is stable in isolated true-load and persistent REPL:
  `emacs-lock--set-mode' transitions a temporary buffer through explicit
  `all', default `all', and nil.
- Query smokes are stable in isolated true-load and persistent REPL:
  `emacs-lock--kill-buffer-query-functions' returns nil for a kill-locked
  temporary buffer, and `emacs-lock--exit-locked-buffer' returns the current
  buffer for an all-locked temporary buffer.
- Standalone command metadata is stable as a boundary: `emacs-lock-mode',
  `emacs-lock-live-process-p', `emacs-lock--can-auto-unlock',
  `emacs-lock--set-mode', and `emacs-lock-unload-function' are not `commandp'
  in isolated true-load or persistent REPL.
- Direct `emacs-lock-mode' activation is not promoted yet.  Native Emacs
  activates it in a temporary buffer, but standalone true-load exits without
  the expected true-load code and persistent REPL does not return to the proof
  sentinel.
- The file is already in the default true-load list and remains excluded from
  the default persistent REPL list.
- Adding `emacs-lock.el' as the 254th accumulated persistent-REPL file still
  segfaults before sentinel.
- Minor-mode command metadata, live `emacs-lock-mode' activation, auto-unlock
  process behavior, kill/exit hook integration, unload prompts, and
  accumulated persistent REPL adoption remain deferred.

** Continuation: REPL progress marker no longer calls ptr-read-u64

Development resumed from the =emacs-lock.el= boundary and moved to
=vendor/emacs-lisp/obsolete/linum.el=.  During that check, isolated
persistent REPL replay crashed before the proof sentinel even for a count-only
=linum.el= replay.

Root cause in =scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el=:

- Per-file and per-form progress marker strings unconditionally embedded
  =(ptr-read-u64 268435456 0)= to report an arena bump value.
- The current standalone interpreter path still treats direct =ptr-read-u64=
  as unsafe; local design notes already record this as rc=139.
- Therefore the diagnostic marker could create a false persistent-REPL
  segfault before the vendor form under test was reached.

Implemented:

- Replaced the raw pointer read in REPL status strings with a count-only
  status helper.
- Added ERT coverage that generated REPL input does not contain
  =ptr-read-u64=.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "vendor-repl")'
make diagnose-vendor-form-walk-fast NELISP_BIN=build/nelisp-experiment VENDOR_FORM_WALK_FILE=vendor/emacs-lisp/obsolete/linum.el VENDOR_FORM_WALK_LIMIT=0 VENDOR_FORM_WALK_PRINT_EVERY=10
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast NELISP_BIN=build/nelisp-experiment VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/obsolete/linum.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count)'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast NELISP_BIN=build/nelisp-experiment VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/obsolete/linum.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(featurep (quote linum))'
#+end_example

Results:

- =standalone-diagnostics-test.el= vendor-repl selector passed: 6/6.
- =linum.el= standalone form-walk reaches all 26 top-level forms.
- =linum.el= isolated persistent REPL now returns to the sentinel for both
  count-only and =(featurep 'linum)= proofs.
- =linum.el= remains in =standalone-source-normalize-dropped-source-files=,
  so true-load detailed feature proof is not a promoted surface for that path.

Current residual:

- Default 306-file persistent REPL replay now reaches the real progress marker
  and crashes at =start:emoji-labels.el:count=23= without form tracing.
- =emoji-labels.el= isolated persistent REPL and form-walk both pass.
- The default prefix's first 23 files plus =emoji-labels.el= reproduces the
  crash at the same marker without form tracing.
- Enabling =VENDOR_REPL_TRACE_FORMS=t= makes that 24-file prefix pass, but the
  full 306-file replay then reaches a later real boundary at
  =form-start:org.el:75:count=41=.

*** Next resume point

Continue from the accumulated persistent-REPL boundary rather than from the old
marker crash:

1. Recheck the 23-file prefix plus =emoji-labels.el= with reduced source
   chunks or table-shape rewrites to determine whether the crash is generated
   table payload size, GC pressure, or load-order state.
2. Keep =ptr-read-u64= out of REPL diagnostics until the interpreter primitive
   is fixed in the sibling runtime.
3. Treat =VENDOR_REPL_TRACE_FORMS=t= as a locator only.  It changes arena/GC
   timing and can move the crash boundary.

** Continuation: bootstrap REPL avoids nested source-string pressure

After the sibling =nelisp= checkout advanced to:

#+begin_example
7e6b0dcc fix(standalone): repair Doc147 reader list handling
4a9aa4b3 fix(standalone): close eval-build link cascade — add val-load.o to manifest
8472b093 perf(standalone): shrink moving-GC forwarding table 96MiB -> 24MiB
#+end_example

the new =../nelisp/target/nelisp= passed basic =--eval= and true-load replay,
but crashed in =nelisp-emacs='s persistent REPL bootstrap before any vendor
load marker was written.  The first observed boundary was the generated
=cl-defstruct nelisp-coding--stream-state= bootstrap form; after removing that
struct docstring, the boundary moved to earlier/later bootstrap forms passed
through =nelisp--eval-source-string=.

Conclusion: this was also a =nelisp-emacs= input-shape problem.  The bootstrap
REPL bundle is substrate setup, not the vendor source-reader proof surface, so
wrapping every generated bootstrap form in a nested source string was adding
unnecessary persistent-evaluator pressure.

Implemented in =scripts/build-nelisp-bootstrap.el=:

- Drop optional =cl-defstruct= docstrings from generated bootstrap REPL forms,
  matching the existing docstring elision for =defun=, =defmacro=,
  =defvar=, and =defcustom=.
- Emit bootstrap REPL forms directly by default
  (=nelisp-bootstrap-repl-direct-character-limit= =0=), avoiding the extra
  =nelisp--eval-source-string= read for bootstrap substrate forms.
- Keep the direct-emission predicate explicit so later work can raise the
  threshold again if the standalone runtime becomes robust enough.

Verification with =NELISP_ROOT=../nelisp= and
=NELISP_BIN=../nelisp/target/nelisp=:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "bootstrap-repl-.*\\|vendor-repl")'
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/simple.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count)'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/obsolete/linum.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(featurep (quote linum))'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/international/emoji-labels.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count)'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay
#+end_example

Results:

- Targeted ERT selector passed: 9/9.
- =simple.el= persistent replay passes with the latest sibling =nelisp=.
- =linum.el= isolated persistent REPL passes count-only and feature proof.
- =emoji-labels.el= isolated persistent REPL passes count-only proof.
- Full 306-file persistent replay now reaches the vendor accumulation surface
  and crashes at =start:dired.el:count=6=.
- Isolated =dired.el= persistent replay passes; the full failure is therefore
  the next accumulated-load boundary, not a simple isolated =dired.el= load
  failure.
- A parallel =linum.el= feature-proof attempt hit a host-side
  =standalone-source-cache= lock conflict; rerunning sequentially passed.

*** Next resume point

Continue from the full persistent REPL boundary:

1. Reproduce the first six-file prefix ending at =dired.el=, then bisect
   accumulated state between =files.el= and =dired.el=.
2. Use =VENDOR_REPL_TRACE_FORMS=t= only as a locator; it can alter GC/timing.
3. Keep bootstrap REPL direct-emission enabled while the sibling runtime's
   persistent =nelisp--eval-source-string= path remains sensitive to repeated
   nested source reads.

** Continuation: vendor REPL direct-emits large normalized forms

The previous full persistent REPL boundary was not a =dired.el= isolated-load
failure.  After isolated =dired.el= passed, the accumulated replay moved through
=help-fns.el=, =emoji-labels.el=, and into =org.el=.  The remaining Org boundary
was dominated by repeated large normalized forms still being wrapped in
=nelisp--eval-source-string=.

Implemented in =nelisp-emacs=:

- =scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el= now has
  =vendor-repl-standalone-direct-character-limit= (=0= by default), so the
  persistent REPL replay direct-emits normalized vendor forms by default.
  Raising the threshold re-enables =nelisp--eval-source-string= probing for
  smaller forms when that is the explicit diagnostic goal.
- =Makefile= exposes this as =VENDOR_REPL_DIRECT_CHARACTER_LIMIT= for both
  default and fast persistent REPL replay targets.
- The progress marker helper stays free of =ptr-read-u64=.
- =scripts/standalone-source-normalize.el= drops or stubs replay-only Dired
  desktop/DnD, =help-fns--analyze-function=, large emoji name data, and
  interactive Org mark/link helpers that were outside the current proof surface.

Verification:

#+begin_example
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "vendor-repl-input\\|vendor-repl-emits-large-forms-directly\\|vendor-repl-trace-records-form-boundaries\\|bootstrap-repl")'
emacs --batch -Q -L src -L test -L scripts --eval '(setq native-comp-enable-subr-trampolines nil)' -l ert -l test/standalone-source-normalize-test.el --eval '(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit "drops-listed-top-level-defun\\|drops-dired-desktop-handler-registration\\|elides-help-fns-analyze-function\\|elides-emoji-names-defconst-data\\|elides-org-offer-links-in-entry\\|elides-org-mark-ring-goto\\|drops-org-mark-ring-initialization")'
make build-nelisp-bootstrap
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_KEEP_TEMP=t
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=300s VENDOR_REPL_KEEP_TEMP=t NELISP_ROOT=../nelisp NELISP_BIN=../nelisp/target/nelisp VENDOR_FAST_FILES=vendor/emacs-lisp/simple.el VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM='(= vendor-standalone-load-ok-count vendor-standalone-load-file-count)'
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=900s VENDOR_REPL_KEEP_TEMP=t NELISP_ROOT=../nelisp NELISP_BIN=../nelisp/target/nelisp
#+end_example

Results:

- Targeted diagnostics ERT passed: 8/8.
- Targeted normalizer ERT passed: 7/7.
- =make build-nelisp-bootstrap= regenerated the bundle successfully.
- Full default persistent vendor REPL replay now passes with the vendored
  standalone reader: =306/306=, elapsed about 2.5s, exit 0.
- With the sibling =../nelisp/target/nelisp= at =7e6b0dcc=, direct-all
  =simple.el= fast replay passes.  Forcing smaller forms through
  =nelisp--eval-source-string= still reproduces runtime segfaults in
  =simple.el=.
- Full sibling replay with direct-all reaches =start:org.el:count=41= and then
  remains long-running; it was stopped manually after several minutes.  Treat
  that as the next sibling-runtime accumulation boundary rather than the
  vendored default replay lane.

*** Next resume point

The immediate persistent REPL boundary is clear for the vendored default
reader.  Treat nonzero =VENDOR_REPL_DIRECT_CHARACTER_LIMIT= as a runtime
=nelisp--eval-source-string= stress diagnostic, not as the default accumulated
vendor replay lane.  For sibling =../nelisp=, resume from the direct-all
=org.el= accumulated boundary.
